Divine Decree
intermediate
6 min
All Events Are Willed by God
Juwayni argues that all events are willed by God based on the equality of acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's argument that all contingent events are willed by God, based on the equality of divine acts and the logical absurdity of attributing contradictory intentions to God.

Core Idea
God's will is absolute and undifferentiated across all events.

This passage from Imam al-Juwayni's al-Aqida al-Nizamiyya presents a decisive proof that all events—including those from humans that appear evil—are willed by God. Juwayni builds on a previously established principle that God's acts do not differ in quality, and then uses a striking analogy to show the impossibility of attributing contradictory purposes to God. Let us follow his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the full Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own argument structure come through.
Notice the dense style and the use of an analogy.
2
Identify the foundational principle
Juwayni begins by referring to an earlier principle: 'acts do not differ with respect to God'. This means God's acts are all equally beyond human assessment.
This principle leads to uniformity in divine will.
3
Examine the analogy of the master and servant
Juwayni presents a hypothetical: a master gives resources to a servant knowing it will cause him to sin, yet claims he intended good. This is called foolish and contradictory.
The absurdity lies in the mismatch between knowledge and claimed intention.
4
Apply the analogy to God and disbelievers
God provides for disbelievers even though He knows they will use it for evil. If we deny God's will in this, we fall into the same contradiction as the foolish master.
Thus, God absolutely wills all events, including provision for disbelievers.
5
Understand the conclusion
Juwayni concludes that this clarifies one division of permissibility in divine judgments—settling the discussion on divine will.
The passage ends by noting the clarity for those who are granted success.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحادثات كلها مرادة الله تبارك وتعالى، وهذا مقتضب من القاعدة التي ذكرناها آنفا. فإذا تقرر أن الأفعال لا تتفاوت في حق الإله تبارك وتعالى فتعلق الإرادة بها على قضية واحدة لا تختلف، ونخصص هذا الفصل بأمر قاطع منزل على ما يرتضيه مولانا فنقول: أضلكم تنزيل أحكام الله تبارك وتعالى على مجارى أفعال الحكماء. وليس يخفى أن من علم أنه لو أمد عبدا من عبيده بالمال وضروب العدد لفسق وفجر وانتهك الحرمات واقتحم الكبائر والموبقات فلو آمده مع علمه البات في ذلك ثم زعم أنه أراد بامتداده بعتاده أن يستمد به في أبواب الخيرات ويتخذه ذريعة في القربات كانت هذه الإرادة مع العلم بنقيضها مشعرة بنهاية السفه والخبط في العقد، سيما إذا علم أنه لو قطع عنه مادته لاشتغل بما يعنيه، ورب الأرباب يمد الكفار بما يشد أزرهم ويقوي منهم ويكمل عدتهم. وإذا مهدنا المسلك فلا معنى للإطناب بعد وضوح العرض. وقد لاح للموفق ما أردناه. انتهى الغرض في أحد قسمي الجواز في أحكام الإلهية.
All contingent things are willed by God, Blessed and Exalted. This is taken from the principle we mentioned earlier. So if it is established that acts do not differ with respect to God, Blessed and Exalted, then the attachment of will to them is on a single basis, not differing. And we specify this chapter with a decisive matter based on what our Master approves, and we say: It has misled you to apply God's judgments to the courses of the actions of wise people. And it is not hidden that whoever knows that if he were to supply a servant from among his servants with wealth and various equipment, and he would become corrupt, immoral, violate sanctities, and commit major sins and destructive acts—then if he supplies him despite his certain knowledge of that, then claims that he intended by his supply of equipment that he use it for the doors of good deeds and take it as a means for acts of devotion—this will, together with knowledge of its contrary, indicates ultimate foolishness and confusion in doctrine, especially if he knows that if he cut off his means he would occupy himself with what concerns him. And the Lord of lords supplies the disbelievers with what strengthens their support and empowers them and completes their numbers. And when we have paved the path, there is no meaning for verbosity after the clarity of the presentation. And what we intended has become clear to the one who is granted success. The purpose has been completed in one of the two divisions of permissibility in the judgments of divinity.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a proof that all contingent events (الحادثات) are willed by God. Juwayni builds on the earlier principle that God's acts are not differentiated (لا تتفاوت). Since acts are equal, God's will attaches to them uniformly (على قضية واحدة لا تختلف). He then presents a decisive argument: it is foolish for someone to give resources to a servant knowing it will cause him to sin, but then claim he intended good. This is contradictory. Yet God gives resources to disbelievers despite knowing they will use them for sin. This proves that God's will is absolute and not bound by human notions of benefit. The argument is directed against those who try to apply human standards of wisdom to God ('تنزيل أحكام الله على مجارى أفعال الحكماء'). Juwayni concludes that this clarifies one of the two divisions of permissibility in divine judgments (أحد قسمي الجواز في أحكام الإلهية), likely referring to the distinction between what God permits and what He decrees.

Key Terms
الحادثات
الإرادة
رب الأرباب
الكفار
قسمي الجواز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God wills evil in the same sense humans do, subject to moral evaluation.
Correction: Juwayni argues God's will is absolute and not bound by human notions of benefit or morality; He wills all events without contradiction.

Checkpoint
What is the basis for saying that God's will attaches to all acts uniformly?
A) That acts differ in value
B) That acts do not differ with respect to God
C) That humans cannot understand God's will
D) That God's will changes with circumstances

Key Takeaway
God's will is absolute, undifferentiated, and applies to all events equally, as proven by the equality of divine acts and the impossibility of contradictory intentions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness a tragedy or injustice, do you truly believe that it is willed by God with a wisdom beyond your understanding? What specific thought or prayer can you adopt to strengthen that trust when your heart resists?
?
You have been given resources (wealth, time, abilities) that God knew you might misuse. Are you using them in a way that aligns with His will, or are you repeating the pattern of the servant who turned blessings into sin? What is one concrete change you will make today to ensure your resources become means of obedience rather than disobedience?
?
The lesson warns against applying human standards of wisdom to God's actions. Where in your life have you subtly assumed that God should act according to your sense of fairness or logic? Will you surrender that assumption and accept that His will is higher than your understanding? Write down one area where you need to change your mindset.

The Four Pillars of Taklif
Juwayni introduces the chapter and outlines the four pillars of taklif.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four pillars upon which the rational possibility of divine obligation (taklif) rests and the methodological approach Juwayni uses.

Core Idea
Taklif is built on four rational pillars that must be established.

This opening passage from Juwayni's al-'Aqida al-Nizamiyya introduces a new chapter on servitude and the attributes relevant to establishing obligatory demands. He states that the rational discourse on the possibility of taklif rests on four pillars, which he will detail after providing their outline. This lesson clarifies the methodological approach and sets the stage for the detailed treatment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the formal introduction and the mention of four pillars.
The passage uses a concise style typical of kalam texts.
2
Identify the four pillars
The passage states that the discourse is related to four pillars, though they are not listed here. Recall that in the preceding outline (mentioned in the text), the pillars were probably introduced.
The author says 'تقدم رسم ترجمتها' – the outline was previously drawn.
3
Understand the methodological note
Juwayni remarks that an expression before detail may fall short, but when the purpose is clarified, the detail fulfills the intention. This reflects a careful pedagogical approach.
4
Reflect on the need for pillars
Consider why taklif requires a rational justification through pillars. This connects to the broader theological context of divine justice and human responsibility.
This lesson prepares you for the detailed discussion of each pillar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب فى العبودية ، والصفات المرعية في ثبوت الطلبات التكليفية القول فى امكان التكليف وجوازه عقلا يتعلق بأربعة أركان نذكرها مفضلة ، وتقدم رسم ترجمتها ، قال العبارة قبل التفصيل قد يقعد عن بعضها ، واذا وضح الغرض يذكر تفصيلها ، فهو الوفاء بالمقصود . الركن الأول : في قدرة العبد ، وتأثيرها في مقدورها . فنقول : قد تقرر عند كل حاط بعقله ، مرقى عن مراتب التقليد في قواعد التوحيد : أن الرب سبحانه وتعالى مطالب عباده بأعمالهم في حياتهم ، وداعيهم اليها ، ومثيبهم ومعاقبهم عليها في مالهم ، وتبين بالنصوص التي لا تتعرض للتأويلات أنه أقدرهم على الوفاء بما طالبهم به ومكنهم من التواصل الى امتثال الأمر ، والانكفاف عن مواقع الزجر ، ولو ذهبت أتلو الآى المتضمنة لهذه المعانى لطال المرام ، ولا حاجة الى ذلك مع قطع اللبيب المنصف به ، ومن نظر فى كتب الشرائع ، وما فيها من الاستحثاث على المكرمات ، والزواجر عن الفواحش الموبقات ، وما فيط ببعضها من الحدود والعقوبات ثم تلفت على الوعد والوعيد ، وما يجب عقده من تصديق المرسلين فى الانباء عما يتوجه على المردة والعتاة من الحساب والعقاب وسوء المنقلب والمـآب ، وقول الله تبارك وتعالى لهم : لم عدتيم وعصيتم وأبيتم ، وقد أرخيت لكم الطول وفسحت لكم المهل وأرسلت الرسل ، وأوضحت المحجة لئلا يكون للناس على الله حجة تتعقد
Chapter on servitude and the observed attributes regarding the establishment of obligatory demands. The statement on the possibility of taklif and its permissibility rationally is related to four pillars which we will detail, and we have preceded their outline. He said: the expression before detail may fall short of some of it, and when the purpose is clarified, its detail is mentioned, so that is fulfilling the intended. The first pillar: on the power of the servant and its effect on its object. We say: it is established for every one who guards his intellect, elevated from the ranks of taqlid in the foundations of tawhid, that the Lord, Glorified and Exalted, is the One who demands of His servants their deeds in their lives, and calls them to them, and rewards and punishes them for them in their future state, and it is made clear by the texts that are not subject to interpretations that He empowered them to fulfill what He demanded of them and enabled them to reach obedience to the command and restraint from the places of prohibition. If I were to recite the verses containing these meanings, the discourse would be long, and there is no need for that with the discerning and fair-minded person. And whoever looks into the books of the divine laws, and what is in them of encouragement to noble deeds and prohibitions from mortal sins, and what is explained in some of them of fixed punishments and penalties, then he considers the promise and threat, and what must be maintained of believing the messengers regarding the news of what is directed at the rebels and the obstinate of the reckoning, punishment, evil end and return, and the saying of God, Blessed and Exalted, to them: 'Why did you transgress and disobey and refuse, while I had extended for you the tether and given you respite and sent the messengers and made clear the path, so that people would have no argument against God' becoming firm.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter on servitude ('ubudiyya) and the attributes observed regarding the establishment of obligatory demands (talabat taklifiyya). The author states that the discourse on the possibility (imkan) and rational permissibility (jawaz 'aqlan) of taklif (divine obligation) rests on four pillars (arkan). He will detail them after first providing an outline. He notes that an expression before detail may fall short, but when the purpose is clarified, the detail fulfills the intention. Then he begins the first pillar: on the power (qudra) of the servant and its effect (ta'thir) on its object (maqdur). The author argues that it is established for anyone who uses his intellect and rises above taqlid in the foundations of tawhid that Allah, the Lord, holds His servants accountable for their deeds in this life, calls them to them, and will reward or punish them for them in the hereafter. The revealed texts (nusus) that are not subject to interpretive manipulation show that Allah empowered them to fulfill what He demanded and enabled them to attain obedience and avoid disobedience. The author says he could cite many Quranic verses but it is unnecessary for the discerning person. He then appeals to observation of the revealed laws (shara'i') which contain encouragements to good deeds and prohibitions from sins, along with fixed penalties, as well as the promise and threat, and the necessity of believing the messengers' reports about the reckoning and punishment for the rebellious. He quotes a paraphrase of a Quranic verse (similar to 4:165) where Allah says to the disbelievers: 'Why did you transgress and disobey, while I gave you respite, sent messengers, and clarified the path, so that people would have no argument against Allah.' The passage ends with 'becoming firm' (tata'aqqad), possibly the start of a new sentence. This first pillar establishes that the servant has genuine power (qudra) and ability to act, which is a key premise for the justice of divine obligation.

Key Terms
تكليف
أركان
امكان
جواز عقلا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many pillars is the rational discourse on taklif related to according to Juwayni?
A) Two
B) Four
C) Five
D) Three

Key Takeaway
The rational possibility of divine obligation rests on four foundational pillars that must be examined in detail.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your obligations from Allah are based on rational pillars, or do you sometimes view them as arbitrary commands? How does this understanding change your attitude towards obeying them?
?
If taklif is rationally grounded, what excuse do you have for neglecting your duties? Can you justify your shortcomings by claiming they are beyond reason?
?
The author emphasizes that the detail fulfills the intended purpose. In your own life, do you seek to understand the details of what Allah has obligated, or are you content with a superficial understanding? What steps will you take to learn the deeper rationale behind His commands?

Divine Decree

The First Pillar: Servant's Power
Juwayni expounds the first pillar on the servant's power and its effect on its objects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the servant's power (qudra) is the first pillar of taklif and how it is established through reason and revelation.

Core Idea
The servant's power is a gift from God, enabling genuine accountability.

In the first pillar, Juwayni argues that the servant's power and its effect on actions are foundational to divine obligation. He establishes that God holds servants accountable for their deeds, empowers them, and makes this clear through texts and the structure of revelation. This lesson unpacks the rational and scriptural evidence he presents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the first pillar
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the definition and the arguments that follow.
The passage is longer than the previous lesson; take your time.
2
Identify the key claims
Juwayni claims that it is rationally established that God demands deeds, rewards/punishes, and that texts show He empowered servants to fulfill demands. Find these claims in the text.
3
Examine the evidence presented
The author uses both rational and scriptural evidence: rational for the intelligent, and scriptural from texts and the structure of sharia. Note how he appeals to the books of divine laws and prophetic reports.
He also quotes a Quranic verse (paraphrased).
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this pillar is first: without genuine human power, taklif would be unjust. The passage shows that empowerment from God is clear from revelation and reason.
This leads to the conclusion that humans can be justly held accountable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب فى العبودية ، والصفات المرعية في ثبوت الطلبات التكليفية القول فى امكان التكليف وجوازه عقلا يتعلق بأربعة أركان نذكرها مفضلة ، وتقدم رسم ترجمتها ، قال العبارة قبل التفصيل قد يقعد عن بعضها ، واذا وضح الغرض يذكر تفصيلها ، فهو الوفاء بالمقصود . الركن الأول : في قدرة العبد ، وتأثيرها في مقدورها . فنقول : قد تقرر عند كل حاط بعقله ، مرقى عن مراتب التقليد في قواعد التوحيد : أن الرب سبحانه وتعالى مطالب عباده بأعمالهم في حياتهم ، وداعيهم اليها ، ومثيبهم ومعاقبهم عليها في مالهم ، وتبين بالنصوص التي لا تتعرض للتأويلات أنه أقدرهم على الوفاء بما طالبهم به ومكنهم من التواصل الى امتثال الأمر ، والانكفاف عن مواقع الزجر ، ولو ذهبت أتلو الآى المتضمنة لهذه المعانى لطال المرام ، ولا حاجة الى ذلك مع قطع اللبيب المنصف به ، ومن نظر فى كتب الشرائع ، وما فيها من الاستحثاث على المكرمات ، والزواجر عن الفواحش الموبقات ، وما فيط ببعضها من الحدود والعقوبات ثم تلفت على الوعد والوعيد ، وما يجب عقده من تصديق المرسلين فى الانباء عما يتوجه على المردة والعتاة من الحساب والعقاب وسوء المنقلب والمـآب ، وقول الله تبارك وتعالى لهم : لم عدتيم وعصيتم وأبيتم ، وقد أرخيت لكم الطول وفسحت لكم المهل وأرسلت الرسل ، وأوضحت المحجة لئلا يكون للناس على الله حجة تتعقد

The statement on the possibility of taklif and its permissibility rationally is related to four pillars which we will detail, and we have preceded their outline. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think human actions are completely coerced by God, making reward and punishment meaningless.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what is the first pillar of taklif?
A) The existence of divine commands
B) The power of the servant and its effect on its object
C) The sending of messengers
D) The promise of reward and threat of punishment

Key Takeaway
The first pillar of taklif is that the servant possesses a genuine power (qudra) from God to act, which is essential for just divine obligation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you actually believe that God has given you the power to avoid it, or do you quietly excuse yourself by thinking 'I can't help it'? What specific sin will you consciously strive against this week, relying on the power God has given you?
?
Juwayni says the texts are clear and not open to interpretation—are there any commands in the Quran you have been 'interpreting' as too difficult or optional to avoid accountability? Name one and commit to acting on it today.
?
If you truly internalize that God has empowered you and removed every excuse, what is one area of your life where you have been making excuses instead of obeying? Write down a concrete step you will take before the day ends.

Divine Decree

The First Pillar: Human Power and Its Effect
Juwayni introduces the first pillar on human capacity and its role in moral obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Juwayni establishes human freedom and responsibility as the necessary foundation for moral obligation (taklīf).

Core Idea
Human actions are truly our own; otherwise, reward and punishment would be unjust.

Juwayni begins the discussion of moral obligation by affirming that humans possess real power and choice. Without this foundation, the entire structure of divine commands, rewards, and punishments would collapse. In this passage, he presents both rational and scriptural evidence that actions occur by our own preference, choice, and capability.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Pay attention to Juwayni's opening structure: he mentions four pillars, then focuses on the first.
2
Identify the core claim
Juwayni asserts that it is established for anyone who uses their intellect that God empowers servants to fulfill what He demands. Find this assertion and note the rational basis he gives.
The claim is that humans have real power (qudra) and effect (ta'thīr) on their actions.
3
Examine the scriptural evidence
List the types of evidence Juwayni cites from revelation: commands, prohibitions, penalties, promises, threats, and the sending of messengers. Notice how he uses the verse 'so that people would have no argument' to show that God has removed excuses.
He does not quote specific verses but refers to the cumulative force of many texts.
4
Understand the conclusion
Juwayni concludes that anyone who doubts human agency despite this evidence is either mentally deficient or blindly following ignorance. Reflect on why this conclusion is so strong in his argument.
This sets the stage for the other pillars and the overall defense of human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في العبودية، والصفات المرعية في ثبوت الطلبات التكليفية. القول في إمكان التكليف وجوازه عقلا يتعلق بأربعة أركان نذكرها مفضلة، وتقدم رسم ترجمتها، قال العبارة قبل التفصيل قد يقعد عن بعضها، وإذا وضح الغرض يذكر تفصيلها، فهو الوفاء بالمقصود. الركن الأول: في قدرة العبد وتأثيرها في مقدورها. فنقول: قد تقرر عند كل حاط بعقله، مرقى عن مراتب التقليد في قواعد التوحيد: أن الرب سبحانه وتعالى مطالب عباده بأعمالهم في حياتهم، وداعيهم إليها، ومثيبهم ومعاقبهم عليها في مالهم، وتبين بالنصوص التي لا تتعرض للتأويلات أنه أقدرهم على الوفاء بما طالبهم به ومكنهم من التواصل إلى امتثال الأمر، والانكفاف عن مواقع الزجر. ولو ذهبت أتلو الآي المتضمنة لهذه المعاني لطال المرام، ولا حاجة إلى ذلك مع قطع اللبيب المنصف به. ومن نظر في كتب الشرائع، وما فيها من الاستحثاث على المكرمات، والزواجر عن الفواحش الموبقات، وما فيها من الحدود والعقوبات، ثم التفت إلى الوعد والوعيد، وما يجب عقده من تصديق المرسلين في الأنباء عما يتوجه على المردة والعتاة من الحساب والعقاب وسوء المنقلب والمآب، وقول الله تبارك وتعالى لهم: لم عديتهم وعصيتم وأبيتم، وقد أرخيت لكم الطول وفسحت لكم المهل وأرسلت الرسل، وأوضحت المحجة لئلا يكون للناس على الله حجة بعد الرسل. فمن أحاط بذلك كله ثم استراب في أن أفعال العباد واقعة على حسب إيثارهم واختيارهم واقتدارهم، فهو مصاب في عقله، أو مستقر على تقليده، مصمم على جهله.
Chapter on servitude and the observed attributes in the establishment of obligatory demands. The statement on the possibility of obligation and its intellectual permissibility relates to four pillars which we will mention in detail, preceded by a sketch of their outline; the statement before detail may omit some, and when the purpose becomes clear, its detail is mentioned, thus fulfilling the objective. The first pillar: on the power of the servant and its effect on what is within his power. We say: It is established for every one who guards his intellect, rising above the ranks of blind following in the foundations of tawḥīd, that the Lord, exalted and high, demands of His servants their deeds in their lives, calls them to them, rewards and punishes them for them in their afterlife; and it is made clear by texts that are not subject to esoteric interpretation that He empowered them to fulfill what He demanded of them and enabled them to attain compliance with the command and abstention from the sites of prohibition. Were I to recite the verses comprising these meanings, the discourse would become lengthy, and there is no need for that given the conviction of the fair-minded intelligent person. And whoever examines the books of revealed laws, and what they contain of incitement to noble deeds, and deterrents from destructive abominations, and what they contain of prescribed penalties and punishments, then turns to the promise and threat, and what must be held of belief in the messengers regarding the news of what awaits the rebellious and obstinate of reckoning, punishment, and evil end and return, and the saying of God, blessed and exalted, to them: 'Why did you transgress and disobey and refuse, while I extended respite for you and granted you delays and sent the messengers, and made clear the path, so that people would have no argument against God after the messengers?' Then whoever encompasses all of that, then doubts that the actions of servants occur according to their preference, choice, and capability, he is afflicted in his intellect or settled upon his blind following, determined in his ignorance.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a chapter on moral obligation and its intellectual foundations. Juwayni first states that the discussion of the possibility of moral obligation (taklīf) rests on four pillars, which he will detail. He then introduces the first pillar: the power of the servant and its effect on what the servant can do. Juwayni argues that it is established for anyone who uses their intellect and rises above blind imitation in the fundamentals of tawḥīd that God holds His servants accountable for their deeds, calls them to obedience, and will reward or punish them. Moreover, the revealed texts clearly show that God gave them the ability to fulfill what was demanded and enabled them to obey and avoid prohibitions. Juwayni then points to the overwhelming evidence from the scriptures: the presence of commandments, prohibitions, prescribed punishments, promises of reward, and threats of punishment, along with the sending of messengers. He cites the verse in which God rebukes the disobedient, highlighting that God gave them respite and sent messengers to remove any excuse. Juwayni concludes that anyone who is aware of all this yet doubts that human actions occur by their own preference, choice, and capability is either mentally deficient or blindly following ignorance. The argument is a cumulative proof from revelation and rational necessity for human freedom and responsibility, against deterministic interpretations.

تأثير
مقدور
تكليف
إيثار
اختيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Juwayni's argument implies that God is not the creator of human actions, reducing His omnipotence.
Correction: Juwayni is not denying divine omnipotence; he is affirming that God gives humans real power and choice, which is the basis for just reward and punishment.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what makes a person who doubts that actions occur by human choice and power to be 'afflicted in intellect'?
A) They rely solely on reason and reject revelation.
B) They are unaware of the clear evidence from scripture and reason.
C) They follow the Ash'ari school of thought.
D) They affirm that God creates all actions directly.

Key Takeaway
Juwayni argues that a coherent system of divine command, reward, and punishment requires that humans have genuine power and choice over their actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if your choices shape your eternal destiny, or do you sometimes hide behind the phrase 'maktub' to avoid the weight of responsibility for your sins? What would change if you fully embraced Juwayni's assertion that your actions are truly your own?
?
When you fail to obey a command of Allah, do you reflect on your own preference and choice (īthār and ikhtiyār), or do you almost immediately say, 'It was from Allah's decree'? This lesson says that such an excuse is a sign of intellectual deficiency or blind following. How will you respond to that charge?
?
Juwayni argues that the very structure of revelation—commands, promises, warnings—implies that you have real power. If you believed that with certainty, how would your approach to daily worship and avoiding sin change starting today?

The Middle Path on Human Power and Divine Creation
Juwayni clarifies the middle path between Jabriyya and Qadariyya regarding human power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari middle path on human power: affirming real human choice while maintaining that God creates all actions in accordance with His promise.

Core Idea
God creates the servant's act after the servant's will, fulfilling His promise without compulsion.

Juwayni here clarifies the correct position on human power and divine creation, avoiding both Jabriyya (denial of human agency) and Qadariyya (human independence). He explains that God's custom is to create the act after the servant's genuine will, as shown by the hadith qudsi linking guidance to seeking. This passage sets the middle course that preserves both divine sovereignty and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument. Notice the verse quote and the hadith.
2
Identify the criticized view
Locate where Juwayni states that severe criticism is only for the explicit Jabriyya. Understand who they are (Jahmiyya and followers).
The Jabriyya deny any effect of human power at all.
3
Examine the acceptable positions
Note the three positions that Juwayni mentions as not subject to criticism: attributing the directing of power/will to the servant, effect on description, or effect on essence with God's assistance.
These are positions that preserve some role for human power.
4
Understand the divine custom
Read how Juwayni describes God's custom: He creates the intended action after the servant's will attaches to it, as a subsequent act in essence. This is the middle path.
This realizes genuine choice and responsibility.
5
Analyze the hadith proof
Juwayni cites the hadith qudsi where guidance is conditional on seeking. Notice how this shows that God's act (creating guidance) follows the human act (seeking).
The conclusion: God keeps His promise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعلى هذا نقول : ( وما على المحسنين من سبيل ) ولا يتوجه ذلك التشني الصريح الا الى الجبرية الصرخاء نفاة قدرة العبد مطلقا كالجهمية وأذيالهم. وأما جعل صرف القدرة أو الارادة الى العبد ، أو جمل تأثير قدرة العبد في وصف الفعل دون أصله ، أو في الأصل بمعاونة الله . فساق: وقد جرت عادة الله بمحض فضله على خلق مراد العبد بعد تعلق ارادة العبد به ، بعدية ذاتية تحقيقا لاختياره ومسئوليته ، حيث رتب سبحانه في كتابه أفعال العبد على ارادة العبد نفسه ، وقال في الحديث القدسي : « كلكم ضال الا من هديته فاستهدوني أهدكم » فعلق الهداية على الاستهداء ، وهو طلب الهداية وارادتها . فيخلق الله سبحانه الهداية اذا طلبها العبد وأرادها على مقتضى وعده الكريم ، وهو لا يخلف الميعاد
So we say: (And there is no blame on the doers of good.) And that open criticism is only directed to the explicit Jabriyya, the deniers of the servant's power absolutely, like the Jahmiyya and their followers. As for attributing the directing of power or will to the servant, or [saying that] the effect of the servant's power is in the description of the act without its essence, or in the essence with the assistance of God, then [we say]: The custom of God by His pure grace has proceeded to create the servant's intended action after the servant's will attaches to it, as a subsequent [act] in essence, realizing his choice and responsibility, since He, glorified, arranged in His Book the servant's actions upon the servant's own will. And He said in the hadith qudsi: 'All of you are astray except those I guide, so ask guidance of Me and I will guide you.' So He made guidance dependent on seeking guidance, which is the request and intention of guidance. So God creates guidance when the servant requests and intends it, according to His generous promise, and He does not break the appointment.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage defines the correct middle position regarding human power and divine creation of actions. The author begins by quoting a Quranic verse ('وما على المحسنين من سبيل') to imply that those who follow the correct path are not to be criticized. Then he specifies that the severe criticism (التشني الصريح) is only directed at the explicit Jabriyya, those who deny any human power at all, such as the Jahmiyya. Next, he distinguishes other views that are not subject to this criticism: the attribution of directing power or will to the servant, or saying that the effect of human power is on the description rather than the essence of the act, or on the essence with God's assistance. He then explains the actual divine custom: God creates the servant's intended action after the servant's will attaches to it, in a way that realizes both genuine choice and responsibility. He supports this with a hadith qudsi where guidance is made conditional on seeking it, indicating that God creates guidance in response to the human act of requesting and intending. The conclusion is that God is faithful to His promise and does not break it, implying that human intention has a real role.

Key Terms
قدرة العبد (human power)
الجبرية (Jabriyya)
الإرادة (will)
الهداية (guidance)
الحديث القدسي (hadith qudsi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the middle view denies God's absolute power or implies human independence.
Correction: Juwayni's position affirms that God creates the act after the servant's will, so human power is real but subordinate; God's power is not diminished because the creation of the act is entirely His, but He does so in accordance with His promise and the servant's choice.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni in this passage, what kind of human power view is the target of the severe criticism?
A) Those who affirm full human power and deny divine intervention
B) Those who completely deny any effect of human power (Jabriyya)
C) Those who say human power affects only the description of the act
D) Those who say human power affects the essence with God's assistance

Key Takeaway
God creates the act after the servant's genuine will, fulfilling His promise and preserving human responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your own actions, do you truly believe that your choices are genuine and that God creates the outcome according to your will? How does this belief affect your daily decisions and your sense of responsibility towards Allah?
?
The hadith qudsi says: 'Ask guidance of Me and I will guide you.' Have you sincerely asked Allah for guidance in a matter, expecting His promise to be fulfilled? What prevents you from doing so right now?
?
Consider the middle path: God creates after your will. Do you sometimes fall into the trap of Jabriyya, blaming everything on divine decree when you sin, or into Qadariyya, feeling independent of Allah? How can you internalize the middle path in your repentance and reliance on Allah?

Refuting the Denial of Human Power's Effect
Juwayni refutes the extreme predestinarian objection using the principle of divine faithfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's argument that the claim 'God does as He wills' is misused to deny human accountability, and that revelation confirms God only commands what people are capable of.

Core Idea
Affirming God's absolute power does not allow the denial of human responsibility.

Imam Juwayni begins by identifying a common objection that undermines the purpose of revelation: the claim that human power has no effect at all. This objection, if accepted, would make God's commands meaningless. In this lesson, you will see how Juwayni refutes this by appealing to both reason and transmitted revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice how the objection is presented and how Juwayni immediately qualifies it as a true word misapplied.
2
Identify the objection and Juwayni's response
The objector argues that since God does as He wills, human power need not have an effect. Juwayni counters that this is a misuse of a true principle: God is transcendent above breaking His promise.
The Quranic verse 'He is not asked about what He does' is used out of context.
3
Understand the principle from revelation
Juwayni states that we understand from revelation that God only charges people with what He informs them they are capable of fulfilling. This is the scriptural basis for human accountability.
This principle is crucial: God's commands are always within human capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما جاء به المرسلون، فإن زعم واعم ممن لم يوفق المنهج الرشاد أنه لا أثر لقدرة العبد في مقدوره أصلا، فاذا طولب بمتعلق طلب الله تعالى بفعل العبد تحريما وفرضا ، ذهب فى الجواب طولا وعرضا . وقال : الله أن يفعل ما يشاء ، ولا يتعرض للاعتراض عليه المعترضون ) لا يسأل عما يفعل ، وهم يسألون ( ) الأنبياء ۲۳ ) قيل : ليس لما جئت به حاصل ، كلمة حق أريد بها باطل . نعم يفعل الله ما يشاء ويحكم ما يريد ، ولكن يتقدس عن الخلف ، ونقيض الصدق وقد فهمنا بضرورات العقول من الشرع المنقول : أنه عزت قدرته : طالب عباده بما أخبر أنهم متمكنون من الوفاء به ، ولو يكلفهم الا على مبلغ الطاقة والوسع فى موارد الشرع .. ومن زعم أن لا أثر للقدرة الحادثة في مقدورها ، كما أثر للعلم فى معلومه ، فوجه مطالبة العبد بأفعاله عنده كوجه مطالبته أن يثبت فى نفسه ألوانا وادراكات ، وهذا خروج عن حد الاعتدال الى التزام الباطل والمحال وفيه ابطال الشرع ، ورد ما جاء به النبيون عليهم السلام . فاذ به لزم المصير الى أن القدرة الحادثة تؤثر في مقدورها، واستحال اطلاق القول بأن العبد خالق أعماله فإن فيه الخروج عما درج عليه سلف الأمة واقتحام ورطات الضلال ، ولا سبيل الى المصير الى وقوع فعل العبد بقدرته الحادثة . والقدرة القديمة ، فان الفعل الواحد يستحيل حدوثه بقادرين ، إذ الواحد لا ينقسم ، فإن وقع بقدرة الله سبحانه استقل بها للعبد فلاحتمال صرفها الى جميعها سميت كلية كما يقال : أقبل على العلم بكليته يبغى بجميع قواه وسمى توجيهها وجهة خاصة أرادة جزئية لتحدد الاتجاه فيها فالأولى حقيقة موجودة ، والثانية أمر اعتباری منتزع من بين المريد والمراد ، كباقى المعانى المصدرية ، فلا يكون : لمعنى الكلى والجزئي في مصطلح المناطقة أى مناسبة هنا ليمكن التشغيب بأن الكلى مفقود، والجزئى هو الموجود على خلاف رأي الماتريدية فى الارادة الكلية والجزئية فليتفطن
What the messengers brought. If someone not guided to the right path claims that there is no effect of the servant's power in his possible act at all, then when he is asked about the object of God's demand concerning the servant's act as forbidden and obligatory, he goes on at length in his answer. He says: God does what He wills, and the objectors cannot object to Him – 'He is not asked about what He does, but they are asked' (Quran 21:23). It is said: What you have brought has no substance; it is a true word intended for falsehood. Yes, God does what He wills and decrees what He intends, but He is transcendent above breaking [His promise] and contrary to truthfulness. And we have understood by necessities of intellects from transmitted revelation that He, mighty is His power, demands from His servants what He informed them they are capable of fulfilling; He only charges them to the extent of ability and capacity in the resources of revelation. And whoever claims that the created power has no effect on its possible object, like the effect of knowledge on its known object, then the way of demanding actions from the servant according to him is like demanding that he bring about colors and sensations in himself. This is a departure from the limits of moderation into adhering to falsehood and impossibility, and it entails nullification of revelation and rejection of what the prophets brought. Therefore it necessarily follows that the created power does have an effect on its possible object, but it is impossible to say that the servant is the creator of his actions, for that is departing from the way of the salaf and plunging into pits of misguidance. And there is no way to say that the servant's action occurs by his created power and the eternal power, for one action cannot occur by two agents of power, since the one cannot be divided. If it occurs by God's power, He alone is independent with it – to the servant, because of the possibility of directing it to all [objects], it is called universal (kulliyya), as one says: He took to knowledge with its universality, meaning with all his powers; and the directing of it to a particular direction is called a particular will (irada juz'iyya) to specify the direction. The first is an actual existent, and the second is a conceptual matter derived from between the willer and the willed, like other verbal-derivative meanings. So there is no relevance to the meaning of universal and particular in the logicians' terminology here to allow objection that the universal is non-existent and the particular is existent, contrary to the Maturidi view on universal and particular will – so let one be attentive.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a proof that created human power must have an effect on its object. The author presents a reductio ad absurdum against the view that human power has no effect. First, he sketches the objection: if someone denies any effect, when challenged to explain how God can demand acts that are beyond human ability, he falls back on the claim that God does as He wills and is not questioned. The author retorts that this is a true statement misapplied; God does act as He wills, but He is pure of breaking promises and contradicting truth. Then the author presents the positive proof: reason and revelation together show that God only charges people with what they are capable of doing. If human power were ineffective, demanding actions would be like demanding impossible things (like producing colors in oneself arbitrarily), which is absurd and leads to nullifying the sharia. Therefore, the created power must have an effect. However, the author immediately guards against a dangerous consequence: this does not mean that man creates his own actions, as that would violate the salaf's position. He then addresses the problem of two agents for one action: one action cannot occur by two powers (human and divine) because it is one; if it occurs by God's power alone, then human power's effect is not independent. He then clarifies the nature of will: the universal will (قدرة كلية) is an actual existent, while the particular intention (إرادة جزئية) is a conceptual construct. This refutes any objection that the universal will is non-existent (as logicians might say) against the Maturidi view.

Key Terms
القدرة الحادثة (created power)
الشرع (revelation)
الخلف (breaking promise)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's absolute freedom means He can command the impossible, and human power is irrelevant.
Correction: God is faithful to His promise and truth; He only commands what people are capable of doing.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what does revelation teach us about God's demands?
A) God demands whatever He wishes, regardless of human ability.
B) God only demands what He informs us we are capable of fulfilling.
C) God demands only what is impossible to test faith.
D) God's demands are not related to human capacity.

Key Takeaway
Juwayni establishes that revelation affirms human capacity, refuting the notion that human power is entirely ineffective.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you have failed to obey Allah, do you ever excuse yourself by saying 'Allah willed it so'? How does Juwayni's argument about divine truthfulness expose the flaw in that excuse? Commit to abandoning that evasion today.
?
If you truly believed that Allah only commands what you are capable of doing, how would that change your response to a difficult obligation you are currently avoiding? What is one step you will take this week to act on that belief?
?
The objector used a true verse to justify a false conclusion. Where in your own thinking might you be using a true Islamic principle to avoid personal responsibility? What would it cost you to abandon that excuse?

The Reductio ad Absurdum for Created Power's Effect
Juwayni proves human power has effect via reductio and warns against Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's reductio argument that denying the effect of human power leads to absurd consequences and nullifies the sharia.

Core Idea
If human power had no effect, divine commands would be demands for the impossible.

Having refuted the rhetorical objection, Juwayni now presents a logical argument. He shows that the view that human power has no effect leads to an absurdity: it would make God's commands equivalent to demanding impossible things, which would nullify the entire sharia. This lesson will walk you through that argument and the important caveat that this does not make humans creators of their actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the reductio passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Juwayni uses an analogy: if human power had no effect, demanding actions would be like demanding that a person produce colors in themselves arbitrarily.
2
Identify the absurd consequence
Juwayni says this is 'departure from the limits of moderation into adhering to falsehood and impossibility', and it entails nullification of revelation and rejection of the prophets.
3
Recognize the conclusion and caution
The conclusion is that created power must have an effect. But Juwayni immediately adds that this does not mean the servant is the creator of his actions, as that would be the Qadariyya heresy.
Keep in mind the balance: human power has effect, but not independent creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما جاء به المرسلون، فإن زعم واعم ممن لم يوفق المنهج الرشاد أنه لا أثر لقدرة العبد في مقدوره أصلا، فاذا طولب بمتعلق طلب الله تعالى بفعل العبد تحريما وفرضا ، ذهب فى الجواب طولا وعرضا . وقال : الله أن يفعل ما يشاء ، ولا يتعرض للاعتراض عليه المعترضون ) لا يسأل عما يفعل ، وهم يسألون ( ) الأنبياء ۲۳ ) قيل : ليس لما جئت به حاصل ، كلمة حق أريد بها باطل . نعم يفعل الله ما يشاء ويحكم ما يريد ، ولكن يتقدس عن الخلف ، ونقيض الصدق وقد فهمنا بضرورات العقول من الشرع المنقول : أنه عزت قدرته : طالب عباده بما أخبر أنهم متمكنون من الوفاء به ، ولو يكلفهم الا على مبلغ الطاقة والوسع فى موارد الشرع .. ومن زعم أن لا أثر للقدرة الحادثة في مقدورها ، كما أثر للعلم فى معلومه ، فوجه مطالبة العبد بأفعاله عنده كوجه مطالبته أن يثبت فى نفسه ألوانا وادراكات ، وهذا خروج عن حد الاعتدال الى التزام الباطل والمحال وفيه ابطال الشرع ، ورد ما جاء به النبيون عليهم السلام . فاذ به لزم المصير الى أن القدرة الحادثة تؤثر في مقدورها، واستحال اطلاق القول بأن العبد خالق أعماله فإن فيه الخروج عما درج عليه سلف الأمة واقتحام ورطات الضلال ، ولا سبيل الى المصير الى وقوع فعل العبد بقدرته الحادثة . والقدرة القديمة ، فان الفعل الواحد يستحيل حدوثه بقادرين ، إذ الواحد لا ينقسم ، فإن وقع بقدرة الله سبحانه استقل بها للعبد فلاحتمال صرفها الى جميعها سميت كلية كما يقال : أقبل على العلم بكليته يبغى بجميع قواه وسمى توجيهها وجهة خاصة أرادة جزئية لتحدد الاتجاه فيها فالأولى حقيقة موجودة ، والثانية أمر اعتباری منتزع من بين المريد والمراد ، كباقى المعانى المصدرية ، فلا يكون : لمعنى الكلى والجزئي في مصطلح المناطقة أى مناسبة هنا ليمكن التشغيب بأن الكلى مفقود، والجزئى هو الموجود على خلاف رأي الماتريدية فى الارادة الكلية والجزئية فليتفطن
What the messengers brought. If someone not guided to the right path claims that there is no effect of the servant's power in his possible act at all, then when he is asked about the object of God's demand concerning the servant's act as forbidden and obligatory, he goes on at length in his answer. He says: God does what He wills, and the objectors cannot object to Him – 'He is not asked about what He does, but they are asked' (Quran 21:23). It is said: What you have brought has no substance; it is a true word intended for falsehood. Yes, God does what He wills and decrees what He intends, but He is transcendent above breaking [His promise] and contrary to truthfulness. And we have understood by necessities of intellects from transmitted revelation that He, mighty is His power, demands from His servants what He informed them they are capable of fulfilling; He only charges them to the extent of ability and capacity in the resources of revelation. And whoever claims that the created power has no effect on its possible object, like the effect of knowledge on its known object, then the way of demanding actions from the servant according to him is like demanding that he bring about colors and sensations in himself. This is a departure from the limits of moderation into adhering to falsehood and impossibility, and it entails nullification of revelation and rejection of what the prophets brought. Therefore it necessarily follows that the created power does have an effect on its possible object, but it is impossible to say that the servant is the creator of his actions, for that is departing from the way of the salaf and plunging into pits of misguidance. And there is no way to say that the servant's action occurs by his created power and the eternal power, for one action cannot occur by two agents of power, since the one cannot be divided. If it occurs by God's power, He alone is independent with it – to the servant, because of the possibility of directing it to all [objects], it is called universal (kulliyya), as one says: He took to knowledge with its universality, meaning with all his powers; and the directing of it to a particular direction is called a particular will (irada juz'iyya) to specify the direction. The first is an actual existent, and the second is a conceptual matter derived from between the willer and the willed, like other verbal-derivative meanings. So there is no relevance to the meaning of universal and particular in the logicians' terminology here to allow objection that the universal is non-existent and the particular is existent, contrary to the Maturidi view on universal and particular will – so let one be attentive.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a proof that created human power must have an effect on its object. The author presents a reductio ad absurdum against the view that human power has no effect. First, he sketches the objection: if someone denies any effect, when challenged to explain how God can demand acts that are beyond human ability, he falls back on the claim that God does as He wills and is not questioned. The author retorts that this is a true statement misapplied; God does act as He wills, but He is pure of breaking promises and contradicting truth. Then the author presents the positive proof: reason and revelation together show that God only charges people with what they are capable of doing. If human power were ineffective, demanding actions would be like demanding impossible things (like producing colors in oneself arbitrarily), which is absurd and leads to nullifying the sharia. Therefore, the created power must have an effect. However, the author immediately guards against a dangerous consequence: this does not mean that man creates his own actions, as that would violate the salaf's position. He then addresses the problem of two agents for one action: one action cannot occur by two powers (human and divine) because it is one; if it occurs by God's power alone, then human power's effect is not independent. He then clarifies the nature of will: the universal will (قدرة كلية) is an actual existent, while the particular intention (إرادة جزئية) is a conceptual construct. This refutes any objection that the universal will is non-existent (as logicians might say) against the Maturidi view.

Key Terms
القدرة الحادثة (created power)
المقدور (possible act)
الشرع (revelation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That affirming an effect of human power automatically means humans are creators of their actions (Qadariyya).
Correction: Juwayni explicitly states that the effect of human power is real, but the servant is not the creator of his actions.

Checkpoint
What does Juwayni compare the demand for actions without human power effect to?
A) Demanding that a person change his height
B) Demanding that a person bring about colors and sensations in himself
C) Demanding that a person remember the past
D) Demanding that a person fly

Key Takeaway
Created power must have an effect, but the servant is not the creator of his own actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you choose to obey or disobey God, do you truly believe your choice has a real effect? Or do you sometimes act as if your actions are meaningless because 'everything is from Allah'? What would change in your life if you fully internalized that your power has a real effect but is not independent?
?
If you believe your actions are entirely created by God with no contribution from you, why would God command you? Does that not make His commands like demanding the impossible? How does that affect your sense of accountability before Him?
?
Have you ever caught yourself falling into the Qadariyya mindset—behaving as if you are the independent creator of your successes? Reflect on a specific moment today where you took credit for something good. Could you have done it without God's power? How can you acknowledge both your effort and His sovereignty without leaning to either extreme?

7 min
Two Agents Cannot Act upon One Act
Juwayni discusses the impossibility of two agents for one act and clarifies the nature of will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's argument that a single action cannot be attributed to both divine and human power, and his clarification of universal and particular will.

Core Idea
One action cannot be divided between two agents—either God alone creates it or the human power is effective in a subordinate sense.

Juwayni anticipates a potential confusion: if human power has an effect, how does that relate to God's own creative power? He argues that one action cannot proceed from two independent powers. He then explains the nature of human will, distinguishing between universal capacity and particular intention, and refutes a misunderstanding based on logical terminology. This lesson examines these subtleties.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on two agents
Read the Arabic and translation. Juwayni states that one action cannot occur by two agents of power because it is one and cannot be divided.
This refutes the idea that both God and human contribute to the same act in the same way.
2
Understand the distinction in will
Juwayni explains that the human power is called 'universal' (kulliyya) because it can be directed to all objects, and its particular direction is called 'particular will' (irada juz'iyya). The universal power is an actual existent, while the particular will is a conceptual derivation.
3
Recognize the refutation of the Maturidi view
Juwayni notes that the logicians' distinction between universal and particular (where universal is non-existent) does not apply here, contrary to what the Maturidis claim about will. He emphasizes that the universal power is real.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?
If your capacity to intend (the universal power) is a real gift from God, but the specific direction of your will (the particular intention) is a conceptual shade, does that change how you view your inner motivations? What do you do with the knowledge that your deepest desires are not fully owned by you?
?
Juwayni argues against the Maturidi that universal will is real and particular will is conceptual. How does this affect your prayer life? Do you pray for God to purify your 'universal' capacity rather than just your 'particular' intentions? What would that mean in practice for your next prayer?

The Impossibility of Splitting an Act Between Two Powers
Juwayni refutes the splitting of a single act between two powers via a trilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's argument that a single human act cannot be divided between human and divine power, and the three unacceptable consequences of trying to do so.

Core Idea
A single act is indivisible — to split it is to fall into shirk or deny accountability.

Juwayni tackles a central problem in kalam: how can human acts be both created by God and truly ours? He argues that any attempt to split a single act between two powers leads to absurd conclusions. This passage presents his trilemma, showing that the only way out is to avoid empty labels and grasp the real meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the concise and forceful style of Juwayni's argument.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the trilemma
Juwayni lists three unacceptable positions that result from attempting to split an act. Identify each one and understand why each is false.
The three options are: claiming exclusive creation, denying accountability, and affirming partnership with God.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Juwayni dismisses the idea that mere terminology (like 'acquisition') solves the problem. Why does he insist on 'attaining a meaning'?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَسَقَطَ أَثَرُ الْقُدْرَةِ الْجَادِثَةِ وَيُسْتَحِيلُ أَنْ يَقَعَ بَعْضُهُ بِقُدْرَةِ اللهِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ .. فَإِنَّ الْفِعْلَ الْوَاحِدَ لَا بَعْضَ لَهُ. وَهَذِهِ مَهْوَاةٌ لَا يَسْلَمُ مِنْ غَوَائِلِهَا إِلَّا مُرْشِدٌ مُوَفَّقٌ إِذَا الْمَرْءُ بَيْنَ أَنْ يَسْعَى الِاسْتِبْدَادَ بِالْخَلْقِ، وَبَيْنَ أَنْ يُخْرِجَ نَفْسَهُ عَنْ كَوْنِهِ مُطَالَبًا بِالشَّرَائِعِ، وَفِيهِ إِبْطَالُ دَعْوَةِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ عَلَيْهِمُ السَّلَامُ، وَبَيْنَ أَنْ يُثْبِتَ نَفْسَهُ شَرِيكًا لِلَّهِ تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى فِي إِيجَادِ الْفِعْلِ الْوَاحِدِ، وَهَذِهِ الْأَقْسَامُ بِجُمْلَتِهَا بَاطِلَةٌ، وَلَا يُنْجِي مِنْ هَذَا الْبَحْرِ الْمُلْتَطِمِ ذِكْرُ اسْمٍ مُخْتَصٍّ، وَلَقَبٍ مُجَرَّدٍ مِنْ غَيْرِ تَحْصِيلِ مَعْنًى.
And the effect of the temporal power falls away, and it is impossible that some of it occurs by the power of Allah, Mighty and Majestic... for a single act has no part. And this is a precipice from whose dangers none is saved except a guided guide. Then a person is between: either claiming exclusive creation, or removing himself from being obligated by the laws—and in that is the nullification of the call of the prophets, peace be upon them—or affirming himself as a partner to Allah, Blessed and Exalted, in bringing about the single act. And all of these divisions are false. And one is not saved from this tumultuous sea by the mention of a specific name or a bare title without attaining a meaning.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a proof refuting the possibility that a single human act is partly caused by human power and partly by divine power. Juwayni argues that such a division is impossible because a single act has no parts. He then presents a trilemma: if you attribute the act entirely to human power, that leads to claiming exclusive creation (shirk); if you deny human power entirely, then humans are not accountable for acts, nullifying prophethood; if you split the act between two powers, that makes the human a partner with God in creation. All three outcomes are false. Juwayni concludes that mere terminology (like 'acquisition' without a real meaning) does not resolve the issue.

Key Terms
القدرة الجادثة (al-qudra al-ḥāditha)
الفعل الواحد (al-fiʿl al-wāḥid)
الاستبداد بالخلق (al-istibdād bi-l-khalq)
شرك (shirk)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A human act can be partly caused by human power and partly by divine power.
Correction: Juwayni argues that a single act has no parts, so such division is impossible and leads to shirk or denial of prophethood.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, how many unacceptable outcomes result from splitting an act between human and divine power?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Juwayni demonstrates that any attempt to divide a single act between two agents leads to falsehood, and only a meaningful solution avoids shirk or rejecting prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'I achieved this by my own effort,' forgetting that Allah is the Creator of your actions? How would your heart change if you truly believed every act—even your obedience—comes entirely from Him?
?
When you sin, do you ever excuse yourself by saying, 'It was Allah's decree'? Juwayni says that removing yourself from accountability nullifies the call of the prophets. If you were to stand before them tomorrow, would they accept that excuse?
?
Pride in your worship or charity—does that not make you a partner with Allah in bringing about that good act? This lesson says that is a false division. Will you today repent of any sense of ownership over your deeds and attribute them wholly to Allah, acknowledging you are merely an instrument?

The Kasb Trap: Demanding a Definition
Juwayni traps the claimant that the servant is an acquisitor (muktasib) by demanding a definition of kasb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's dialectical strategy of demanding a definition of 'kasb' and why any attempt to define it leads to the same logical divisions.

Core Idea
Kasb is an empty term unless you can define it without contradiction.

Juwayni now turns to those who say the servant is an 'acquisitor' (muktasib) and that acquisition (kasb) is the effect of his power while Allah is the creator. This sounds like a middle ground, but Juwayni will show it is only a verbal escape. By demanding a precise definition of 'kasb', he will trap the claimant into the same logical trilemma that doomed other positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: a claim is stated, then a counter-question is posed, and then a consequence is announced.
Pay attention to the phrase 'the predetermined divisions are rotated upon him' – these are the inescapable logical options.
2
Identify the claim and Juwayni's counter-question
The claimant says the servant is a 'muktasib' and the effect of his power is 'iktisab', while Allah is the creator. Juwayni asks: 'What is kasb? What is its meaning?' This forces a definition of the key term.
Juwayni is not satisfied with mere terminology; he wants a real meaning.
3
Reflect on why a definition is demanded
By asking for a definition, Juwayni forces the claimant to commit to something specific about how human action relates to divine power. Without a definition, the term 'kasb' is just a placeholder that avoids the real issue.
4
Understand why the divisions are 'inescapable'
Once the claimant tries to define kasb, he will have to choose between options (e.g., kasb as synonymous with creation, or as an independent power, etc.). Earlier proofs showed that all such options are impossible or lead to contradiction, so he cannot escape.
The phrase 'no escape' means the claimant is trapped in the same trilemma.
5
Connect to the broader argument
This passage is a dialectical move that shows 'kasb' is not a solution but a verbal trick. The learner should see how this fits into the overall refutation of human power as independent or as a true cause.
Consider what a viable definition of kasb would need to include to avoid the trilemma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَنْ يَزْعُمُ أَيْضًا وَذَلِكَ أَنَّ قَائِلًا لَوْ قَالَ: الْعَبْدُ مُكْتَسِبٌ. وَأَثَرُ قُدْرَتِهِ الِاكْتِسَابُ، وَالرَّبُّ تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى مُخْتَرِعٌ وَخَالِقٌ لِمَا الْعَبْدُ مُكْتَسِبٌ. قِيلَ لَهُ فَمَا الْكَسْبُ؟ وَمَا مَعْنَاهُ وَأُدِيرَتِ الْأَقْسَامُ الْمُقَدَّرَةُ عَلَى هَذَا الْقَائِلِ، فَلَا يَجِدُ عَنْهَا مَهْرَبًا.
Someone also claims, and that is that if a speaker says: 'The servant is an acquisitor (muktasib). And the effect of his power is acquisition (iktisāb), and the Lord, Blessed and Exalted, is the inventor and creator of what the servant acquires.' It is said to him: 'What is kasb? And what is its meaning?' And the predetermined divisions are rotated upon this speaker, and he finds no escape from them.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents a dialectical move against those who use the term 'acquisition' (kasb) to explain human action while affirming divine creation. Juwayni says that if someone claims the servant is an 'acquisitor' and that the effect of his power is 'acquisition', while Allah is the creator, then we ask him to define kasb. By pressing for a real meaning, the claimant is forced into the same logical divisions (the trilemma mentioned earlier) and cannot escape. The argument is that 'acquisition' is an empty term unless its precise meaning is given, and any meaningful definition will lead back to the same false outcomes.

Key Terms
مُكْتَسِب (muktasib)
الِاكْتِسَاب (al-iktisāb)
الكَسْب (al-kasb)
أَثَرُ الْقُدْرَة (athar al-qudra)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Using the term 'kasb' resolves the problem of human agency and divine creation.
Correction: Juwayni shows that 'kasb' is just a word; without a clear definition that avoids logical contradictions, it does not solve anything.

Checkpoint
What does Juwayni demand from the one who says the servant is an 'acquisitor' (muktasib)?
A) Proof from the Quran
B) A definition of 'kasb'
C) A list of his teachers
D) A confession of sin

Key Takeaway
Juwayni's demand for a definition of 'kasb' reveals that the term is a verbal evasion unless it is given a coherent meaning that escapes the logical divisions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say that your actions are your own while believing in divine decree, are you using a term like 'kasb' to avoid the uncomfortable tension? What would happen if you truly pressed for a definition of how your will and Allah's will coexist?
?
Juwayni shows that an undefined term can be a verbal evasion. In what area of your own faith—perhaps regarding tawakkul or rizq—do you rely on terms you have not deeply defined? Are you hiding from a hard truth?
?
If you were forced to give a precise meaning to how you ‘choose’ while Allah creates, would you find any escape? Does this lesson reveal a need for you to personally grapple with the mystery of qadar rather than settle for convenient phrases?

Consensus and Quranic Proof for Allah as Sole Creator
Juwayni cites consensus and Quranic verses to assert that only Allah is Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Juwayni uses the consensus of early Muslims and Quranic verses to refute the claim that humans create their own actions.

Core Idea
Early consensus and clear verses establish Allah alone as Creator.

Juwayni begins his response to the objection by invoking the authoritative consensus of the early Muslim community, who agreed unanimously that there is no creator but Allah. He then reinforces this with several Quranic verses that explicitly attribute creation to Allah. This lesson examines these foundational proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage containing the objection and Juwayni's first part of the answer. Focus on how he invokes consensus and cites verses.
Notice the phrase 'قُلْنَا' which marks the beginning of the answer.
2
Identify the consensus claim
Juwayni says the Muslims before sects arose agreed that there is no creator but Allah. Understand that this consensus (ijma) is a key proof in Islamic theology.
Consensus is considered authoritative when based on early generations.
3
List the Quranic verses cited
Juwayni provides four verses. Identify each one and note how each emphasizes Allah's exclusive attribute of creation.
The verses are from Surah An-Nahl, Al-An'am, and Fatir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ قِيلَ: لِمَ لَا تَذْكُرُوا قَوْلًا مُقْنِعًا فِي الرَّدِّ عَلَى أَنَّ الْعَبْدَ مُخْتَرِعٌ خَالِقٌ لِأَفْعَالِهِ؟ قُلْنَا: الْمُسْلِمُونَ بِأَجْمَعِ قَاطِبَةٍ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَظْهَرَ الْبِدَعُ وَالْآرَاءُ، وَتَبْغَ أَصْحَابُ الْأَهْوَاءِ: عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَا خَالِقَ إِلَّا اللهُ (تَعَالَى)، كَمَا لَهَجُوا بِأَنَّهُ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ، وَتَمَدَّحَ اللهُ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى بِالْخَلْقِ فِي أَيِّ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ مِنْهَا قَوْلُهُ تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى: (أَفَمَنْ يَخْلُقُ كَمَنْ لَا يَخْلُقُ) (النَّحْلِ ١٧) وَقَوْلُهُ تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى: (خَالِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ) (الْأَنْعَامِ ١٠٢) وَقَوْلُهُ: (خَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ) (الْأَنْعَامِ ١٠١) وَقَوْلُهُ تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى: (هَلْ مِنْ خَالِقٍ غَيْرُ اللهِ) (فَاطِرٍ ٣) وَلَا يَشُكُّ لَبِيبٌ أَنَّ «مَنْ وَصَفَ نَفْسَهُ بِكَوْنِهِ خَالِقًا عَلَى التَّحْقِيقِ فَقَدْ أَعْظَمَ الْفِرْيَةَ» وَأَتَى بِمَا لَوْ نَطَقَ بِهِ نَاطِقٌ فِي الْأَوَّلِينَ لَتَعَرَّضَ لِلْكَبِيرِ الْعَظِيمِ، وَالرَّدِّ الْبَلِيغِ. وَكَيْفَ يُنْصَفُ الْعَبْدُ بِكَوْنِهِ خَالِقًا وَهُوَ لَا يُحِيطُ عِلْمًا بِتَفَاصِيلِ أَفْعَالِهِ، وَمَنْ لَا يَعْلَمُ حَقِيقَةَ مَا صَدَرَ مِنْهُ، وَمَنْ يَخْطُ بِمِقْدَارِهِ وَمَبْلَغِهِ كَيْفَ يَكُونُ خَالِقَهُ؟ وَالْعِلْمُ بِالشَّيْءِ أَقْرَبُ مِنْ خَلْقِهِ. وَهَذَا مَعْنَى قَوْلِهِ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى: (وَأَسِرُّوا قَوْلَكُمْ أَوِ اجْهَرُوا بِهِ. إِنَّهُ عَلِيمٌ بِذَاتِ الصُّدُورِ أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ؟) (الْمُلْكِ ١٣ وَ١٤) فَدَلَّ مُقْتَضَى الْآيَةِ: أَنَّ الْعَالِمَ بِحَقَائِقِ الْحَادِثَاتِ: بَارِئُهَا وَخَالِقُهَا. وَقَدْ تَقَرَّرَ فِي قَضَايَا الْعُقُولِ أَنَّ الْأَفْعَالَ دَالَّةٌ عَلَى عِلْمِ خَالِقِهَا بِهَا. فَإِذَا صَدَرَتْ [؟] أَفْعَالٌ مِنَ الْعَبْدِ فِي حَالَةِ ذُهُولِهِ عَنْهَا، فَهِيَ دَالَّةٌ عَلَى عِلْمِ الْعَبْدِ بِهَا. فَإِنَّهُ غَيْرُ عَالِمٍ بِمَا جَرَتْ يَدُهُ بِهِ فِي حَالِ غَفْلَتِهِ وَذُهُولِهِ. وَالنَّائِمُ غَيْرُ شَاعِرٍ بِتَقَلُّبَاتِهِ فِي غَلَبَاتِ النَّوْمِ، وَغَفَوَاتِهِ. فَإِذَا وَجَبَ أَنْ تَدُلَّ الْأَفْعَالُ عَلَى عِلْمِ خَالِقِهَا، ثُمَّ لَمْ تَدُلَّ عَلَى عِلْمِ الْعَبْدِ فِي حَالِ نَوْمِهِ وَذُهُولِهِ دَلَّ أَنَّهَا دَالَّةٌ عَلَى عِلْمِ خَالِقِهَا وَمُقَدِّرِهَا، وَهُوَ رَبُّ الْعَالَمِينَ.
If it is said: 'Why do you not mention a convincing statement in refutation of the claim that the servant is an inventor and creator of his actions?' We say: The Muslims, all of them together, before the appearance of innovations and opinions, and before the partisans of desires rebelled, agreed that there is no creator but Allah (Exalted), just as they were accustomed that there is no god but Allah. And Allah, Glorified and Exalted, praised Himself with creation in places in the Book, among them His saying, Blessed and Exalted: 'Then is He who creates like one who does not create?' (An-Nahl 17) and His saying, Blessed and Exalted: 'Creator of all things' (Al-An'am 102) and His saying: 'He created all things' (Al-An'am 101) and His saying, Blessed and Exalted: 'Is there any creator other than Allah?' (Fatir 3). And no intelligent person doubts that 'whoever describes himself as being truly a creator has indeed committed the greatest slander' and has come with something which, if a speaker had uttered it among the former peoples, he would have exposed himself to great enormity and forceful rebuttal. And how can the servant be described as being a creator when he does not comprehend knowledge of the details of his actions? And one who does not know the reality of what emanates from him, and one who errs concerning its measure and extent, how can he be its creator? And knowledge of a thing is nearer than its creation. And this is the meaning of His saying, Glorified and Exalted: 'And conceal your speech or publicize it; indeed, He is Knowing of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know?' (Al-Mulk 13-14). So the implication of the verse indicates that the Knower of the realities of contingent things is their Originator and Creator. And it has been established in the judgments of intellects that actions indicate the knowledge of their creator of them. So if actions [?] emanate from the servant in a state of heedlessness of them, they would indicate the servant's knowledge of them. For he is not knowledgeable of what his hand has done in a state of his inattention and heedlessness. And the sleeper is not aware of his movements in the overwhelming states of sleep and its lapses. So if it is necessary that actions indicate the knowledge of their creator, and then they do not indicate the servant's knowledge in the state of his sleep and heedlessness, it indicates that they indicate the knowledge of their Creator and Appointer, and He is the Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector asks why the Ash'aris do not provide a convincing refutation against those who say the servant creates his own actions. Juwayni answers first by citing the consensus of early Muslims that there is no creator but Allah, and he supports this with Quranic verses (16:17, 6:102, 6:101, 35:3). He then argues that claiming to be a creator is a grave slander. Next, he presents a rational proof: a person does not have comprehensive knowledge of all the details of his own actions—he is often unaware of what he does (e.g., in sleep or heedlessness). Since actions indicate the knowledge of their creator, and the servant lacks such knowledge when unaware, the actions cannot be attributed to the servant's creation. Instead, they point to the knowledge of Allah, who is their true Creator. Juwayni invokes Quran 67:13-14 to reinforce that the One who creates is the One who knows all.

Key Terms
خَالِق (khāliq)
إِجْمَاع (ijmāʿ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that consensus is not a strong proof in theological matters or that the Quranic verses do not explicitly exclude human creation.
Correction: In Ash'ari theology, the consensus of the early Muslim community (ijma) is a definitive proof. The Quranic verses clearly state that Allah alone creates, and is not like those who do not create.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what did the early Muslims unanimously agree upon before the appearance of innovations?
A) That the servant is a creator of his actions
B) That there is no creator but Allah
C) That consensus is not a proof
D) That the Quran has many interpretations

Key Takeaway
Early Muslim consensus and Quranic verses overwhelmingly affirm that Allah alone is the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every action you do—every word, every movement—is created by Allah and not by you? Where in your life do you subtly feel you are the originator, and how can you train yourself to attribute all creation to Him alone?
?
The early Muslims were united on 'no creator but Allah.' Are you united with them in your heart, or do you sometimes credit yourself for your successes? Confess one specific achievement you have mentally claimed as your own, and repent for that hidden shirk.
?
Juwayni says claiming to be a creator is the greatest slander. Have you ever, even inwardly, thought you 'made' something happen by your own power? Right now, commit to saying 'Allah created this' every time you accomplish something today.

Divine Decree

The Argument from Ignorance: Why Humans Cannot Be Creators
Juwayni argues that ignorance of one's actions disproves human creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's rational argument that a person's lack of complete knowledge of his own actions proves that he cannot be their creator.

Core Idea
If you don't know your actions fully, you cannot be their creator.

Juwayni moves from scriptural proofs to a rational argument. He contends that a person is often unaware of many aspects of his actions, especially during sleep or heedlessness. Since actions indicate the knowledge of their creator, and the servant lacks such knowledge, his actions must be created by Allah, who knows all.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage from 'وَكَيْفَ يُنْصَفُ الْعَبْدُ' to the end. Note the rational structure: premise, principle, example, conclusion.
Juwayni uses rhetorical questions to build his case.
2
Understand the principle about actions and knowledge
Juwayni states that actions indicate the knowledge of their creator. Grasp this key principle that links creation to knowledge.
This principle is established 'in the judgments of intellects'—it is a rational axiom.
3
Apply the sleep analogy
The sleeper is unaware of his movements. Since he lacks knowledge, his actions cannot indicate his knowledge, so he cannot be the creator. Therefore, the true creator must be Allah who knows all.
This analogy powerfully illustrates the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
