عِلْمِ الْعَبْدِ فِي حَالِ نَوْمِهِ وَذُهُولِهِ دَلَّ أَنَّهَا دَالَّةٌ عَلَى عِلْمِ خَالِقِهَا وَمُقَدِّرِهَا، وَهُوَ رَبُّ الْعَالَمِينَ.
If it is said: 'Why do you not mention a convincing statement in refutation of the claim that the servant is an inventor and creator of his actions?' We say: The Muslims, all of them together, before the appearance of innovations and opinions, and before the partisans of desires rebelled, agreed that there is no creator but Allah (Exalted), just as they were accustomed that there is no god but Allah. And Allah, Glorified and Exalted, praised Himself with creation in places in the Book, among them His saying, Blessed and Exalted: 'Then is He who creates like one who does not create?' (An-Nahl 17) and His saying, Blessed and Exalted: 'Creator of all things' (Al-An'am 102) and His saying: 'He created all things' (Al-An'am 101) and His saying, Blessed and Exalted: 'Is there any creator other than Allah?' (Fatir 3). And no intelligent person doubts that 'whoever describes himself as being truly a creator has indeed committed the greatest slander' and has come with something which, if a speaker had uttered it among the former peoples, he would have exposed himself to great enormity and forceful rebuttal. And how can the servant be described as being a creator when he does not comprehend knowledge of the details of his actions? And one who does not know the reality of what emanates from him, and one who errs concerning its measure and extent, how can he be its creator? And knowledge of a thing is nearer than its creation. And this is the meaning of His saying, Glorified and Exalted: 'And conceal your speech or publicize it; indeed, He is Knowing of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know?' (Al-Mulk 13-14). So the implication of the verse indicates that the Knower of the realities of contingent things is their Originator and Creator. And it has been established in the judgments of intellects that actions indicate the knowledge of their creator of them. So if actions [?] emanate from the servant in a state of heedlessness of them, they would indicate the servant's knowledge of them. For he is not knowledgeable of what his hand has done in a state of his inattention and heedlessness. And the sleeper is not aware of his movements in the overwhelming states of sleep and its lapses. So if it is necessary that actions indicate the knowledge of their creator, and then they do not indicate the servant's knowledge in the state of his sleep and heedlessness, it indicates that they indicate the knowledge of their Creator and Appointer, and He is the Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector asks why the Ash'aris do not provide a convincing refutation against those who say the servant creates his own actions. Juwayni answers first by citing the consensus of early Muslims that there is no creator but Allah, and he supports this with Quranic verses (16:17, 6:102, 6:101, 35:3). He then argues that claiming to be a creator is a grave slander. Next, he presents a rational proof: a person does not have comprehensive knowledge of all the details of his own actions—he is often unaware of what he does (e.g., in sleep or heedlessness). Since actions indicate the knowledge of their creator, and the servant lacks such knowledge when unaware, the actions cannot be attributed to the servant's creation. Instead, they point to the knowledge of Allah, who is their true Creator. Juwayni invokes Quran 67:13-14 to reinforce that the One who creates is the One who knows all.

Key Terms
إِحَاطَة عِلْم (iḥāṭa ʿilm)
تَفَاصِيل أَفْعَال (tafāṣīl afʿāl)
دَلَالَة الْأَفْعَال (dalālat al-afʿāl)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if a person consciously intends an act, he knows it fully and therefore can be a creator of that act.
Correction: Juwayni shows that even in conscious acts, we lack comprehensive knowledge of all details, and during sleep we have no knowledge at all. Thus, the rational principle that actions indicate the knowledge of their creator cannot be attributed to the servant, so the true creator must be Allah.

Checkpoint
What does Juwayni use as an example to show that the servant does not have complete knowledge of his actions?
A) The state of a sleeping person
B) The state of a praying person
C) The state of a person reciting Quran
D) The state of a person in certainty

Key Takeaway
Lack of full knowledge of one's actions proves that the true Creator is Allah alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a moment today when you acted without full awareness—maybe you spoke harshly in a flash of anger or scrolled through your phone during a conversation. In that moment, did you really know the full measure of what you were doing? If not, how can you claim to be its creator? And if you are not, who is ultimately responsible? Will you repent for that action and rely on Allah's mercy?
?
You believe you know yourself better than anyone. But Juwayni says you don't even know the details of your own actions. What does this say about your pride in your intentions and plans? Does it humble you to admit that Allah alone fully knows what you do? What needs to change in your heart?
?
Every movement you make, even in sleep, is recorded and known by Allah. Yet you often forget that He sees you. If you truly believed that your lack of knowledge proves you are not the creator—and that He is—would you live today differently? Write down one specific habit you will change because of this truth.

The True Doctrine: Servant's Power is Created, Act Attributed to Allah
Juwayni responds to an objection by stating the correct doctrine of divine creation and human acquisition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position that the servant's power is created by Allah and that the act is ultimately attributed to Allah, not the servant.

Core Idea
The servant's power is created; the act belongs to Allah.

Juwayni has been refuting various sectarian views on the nature of divine speech and human action. Now an objector demands that he state the truth plainly. In response, Juwayni articulates the core Ash'ari doctrine: the servant's power (qudra) is created by Allah, and although the act occurs through that power, it is attributed to Allah as the ultimate creator. This lesson unpacks that concise statement.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the objector challenges Juwayni and how Juwayni responds.
The objector's claim is that Juwayni has only negated other views.
2
Identify the two claims
Juwayni makes two key claims: (1) the servant's power is created by Allah, and (2) the act occurs by that power but is attributed to Allah. Understand each.
The phrase 'bi-ittifāq al-ʿālamīn bi-l-ṣāniʿ' means by agreement of all who affirm a Creator.
3
Reflect on the balance
Think about why Juwayni insists the act is attributed to Allah even though it occurs by the servant's power. This is the Ash'ari theory of kasb (acquisition).
The servant's power is effective but not creative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ قِيلَ: مَا ذَكَرْتُمُوهُ إِبْطَالٌ مِنْكُمْ لِأَقْسَامِ الْكَلَامِ وَتَتَبُّعٌ لِلْمَذَاهِبِ وَلَمْ تُوَضِّحُوا مَا هُوَ الْحَقُّ بَعْدُ. قُلْنَا: لَيْسَ بِمُدْرَكِ الْحَقِّ خَفَاءٌ لِمَنْ وُفِّقَ لَهُ. وَهَا نَحْنُ نُبْدِيهِ بِالْحُرِّيَّةِ مِنْ غَيْرِ تَعْرِيضٍ وَتَعْرِيجٍ عَلَى تَقَلَّبٍ فَنَقُولُ: قُدْرَةُ الْعَبْدِ مَخْلُوقَةٌ لِلَّهِ تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى بِاتِّفَاقِ الْعَالَمِينَ بِالصَّانِعِ، وَالْفِعْلُ الْمَقْدُورُ بِالْقُدْرَةِ الْحَادِثَةِ وَاقِعٌ بِهَا قَطْعًا، وَلَكِنَّهُ مُضَافٌ إِلَى اللهِ تَبَارَكَ.
If it is said: 'What you have mentioned is a nullification of the divisions of speech and a pursuit of sects, and you have not clarified what the truth is yet.' We say: The attainment of truth is not hidden for one who is guided to it. And here we will show it freely without equivocation or deviation upon fluctuation. So we say: The servant's power is created by Allah, Blessed and Exalted, by the agreement of all who know the Maker, and the act that is empowered by the temporal power occurs by it certainly, but it is attributed to Allah, Blessed and Exalted.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector claims that Juwayni's previous discussion only refutes other views but does not state the truth. Juwayni replies that the truth is not hidden for the guided, and he then expounds the correct position: The servant's power (qudra) is created by Allah, as agreed upon by all who affirm a Maker (i.e., Muslims and theists). The act that is performed by this temporal power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha) indeed occurs by that power—meaning the power is effective—but the act is ultimately attributed to Allah (as the creator and originator). This is the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb: the act is created by Allah and acquired by the servant through a power that is itself created.

Key Terms
قُدْرَة الْعَبْد
الْقُدْرَة الْحَادِثَة
مَخْلُوقَة
مُضَاف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if the act occurs by the servant's power, then the servant is the creator of the act, or that the power is independent.
Correction: Juwayni clarifies that the power itself is created by Allah, and the act remains attributed to Allah as the ultimate creator, not the servant.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni's final statement, to whom is the act attributed?
A) The servant
B) The servant's power
C) Allah
D) Both servant and Allah

Key Takeaway
Juwayni's final position is that the servant's power is created by Allah, and the act, though effected by that power, is attributed to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make a decision today, will you pause to acknowledge that your ability to choose and act is itself a gift created by Allah? How would this awareness change your sense of dependence on Him?
?
If your every act is ultimately attributed to Allah, what does that imply about your accountability? When you sin, do you truly feel that you are misusing a power that Allah created, and that you must repent to Him who owns the act?
?
The truth Juwayni states is that your power is not your own—it is created and sustained by Allah moment by moment. Does your heart live in that reality? What one habit can you start today to remind yourself of this truth before you act?

Human Power and Divine Creation: Juwayni's Response
Juwayni responds to an objection by affirming that human power is created and acts are from God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari doctrine that human power is created by God and acts are attributed to God's determination and creation, resolving the tension between human agency and divine omnipotence.

Core Idea
Human power is God's creation; acts occur by it yet are attributed to God alone.

In this passage, an objector accuses Juwayni of merely negating other views without stating the truth. Juwayni responds directly and clearly, laying out the Ash'ari position on human power and its relation to divine creation. This lesson unpacks that response and explains how human acts can be both from a created power and entirely dependent on God.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection: the critic claims Juwayni has only invalidated classifications without clarifying the truth. Notice the tone of challenge.
This sets up the need for a positive statement of doctrine.
2
Juwayni's confident reply
Juwayni asserts that the truth is clear to those whom God guides, and he will present it plainly. This shows his certainty and authority.
He prefaces his statement with a declaration of clarity.
3
The core doctrine stated
Read the central claim: the servant's power is created by God, the act occurs by that power, but it is attributed to God as determination and creation. Understand the two aspects: occurrence by the servant's power and attribution to God.
This is the key resolution of the problem.
4
Clarification on power and attribute
Juwayni explains that the power itself is not the servant's act but his attribute, and it belongs to God. The act occurs by God's act (power), and since the locus is God's creation, the act is attributed to God's creation.
This prevents misunderstanding that the servant's power is independent.
5
Synthesize the doctrine
Combine the points: the servant has a real, effective power that is created by God, and the acts that occur by it are ultimately created and determined by God. This is the Ash'ari middle path.
Contrast with Qadariyya (human creates his own act) and Jabriyya (no human power).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان قيل : ما ذكرتموه ابطال منكم لأقسام الكلام وتتبع للمذاهب ولم توضحوا ما هو الحق بعد . قلنا : ليس بمدرك الحق خفاء لمن وفق له . وها نحن نبديه بالحرية من غير تعريض وتعريج على تقلب فنقول : قدرة العبد مخلوقة الله تبارك وتعالى باتفاق العالمين بالصانع ، والفعل المقدور بالقدرة الحادثة واقع بها قطعا ، ولكنه مضاف الى الله تبارك وتعالى تقديرا وخلقا . فإن وقع يفعل الله تبارك وتعالى وهو القدرة ، وليست القدرة فعلا للعبد ، وأنما هي صفته ، وهى ملك الله تبارك وتعالى وخلق الله ، واذا كان موقع الفعل خلقا الله ، فالواقع به مضاف خلقة الرب خلق تبارك وتعالى . وتقدير
For it is said: 'What you have mentioned is a nullification of the divisions of discourse and a pursuit of schools, and you have not clarified what the truth is after all.' We say: 'The truth is not obscure to one who is granted success to it. And now we will present it freely without deviation or turning aside.' So we say: The servant's power is created by God, Blessed and Exalted, by agreement of those who know the Maker, and the act empowered by the contingent power occurs by it decisively, but it is attributed to God, Blessed and Exalted, as determination and creation. For the occurrence occurs by the act of God, Blessed and Exalted, which is power, and the power is not an act of the servant; rather it is his attribute, and it is the possession of God and the creation of God. And since the locus of the act is the creation of God, that which occurs by it is attributed to the creation of the Lord, Blessed and Exalted, as creation. And determination.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer followed by a doctrinal statement on human power (qudra) and divine creation. The objector accuses Juwayni of merely invalidating classifications without stating the truth. Juwayni replies that the truth is clear to those whom God guides, and he will present it plainly. He then states the Ash'ari doctrine: The servant's power (qudra) is created by God. The act that is empowered by this created power occurs by means of that power, but the act is attributed to God in terms of determination (taqdir) and creation (khalq). He explains further: The occurrence is by God's act, which is power itself; the power in the servant is not his act but his attribute, and it belongs to God. Since the locus of the act is God's creation, the act that occurs is attributed to God's creation. Thus, human acts are both from the servant's acquired power and from God's creative act, without contradiction.

Key Terms
قدرة
فعل
خلق
تقدير
عبد
رب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Ash'aris deny all human power and reduce humans to mere puppets.
Correction: Juwayni affirms that the servant has a real power (qudra) created by God, and the act occurs by that power. However, the power itself and its effect are ultimately from God's creation. This preserves human responsibility while maintaining divine sovereignty.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what is the relationship between the servant's power and the act?
A) The servant's power creates the act independently.
B) The servant's power is created by God, and the act occurs by it but is attributed to God's creation.
C) The servant has no power over his actions.
D) The act is solely God's action with no involvement of the servant.

Key Takeaway
Juwayni affirms that human power is created by God, and while acts occur through that power, they are ultimately attributed to God's determination and creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what area of your life do you act as if your own power is independent of God? How does it change your attitude to realize that even your ability to act is created by Him?
?
When you sin, do you blame your own weakness or do you recognize that even that sin occurs within God's determination? How does this affect your repentance and your reliance on His mercy?
?
If every act of yours is ultimately attributed to God's creation, how does this shape your gratitude for the good deeds you perform? Do you take credit or acknowledge His giving?

The Created Power in the Servant
Juwayni defines human power as created attribute existing before action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that in Ash'ari theology, human power (qudra) is a created attribute from Allah that truly exists in the servant before the action, and that denying this is obstinacy.

Core Idea
Human power is real but created – a gift from Allah, not our own making.

Imam Juwayni begins by clarifying a foundational point in Ash'ari kalam: the power by which we act is not something we produce. It is an attribute that Allah creates in us. This lesson walks through the key claim and its supporting arguments, including a surprising analogy from nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of power
Read the first part of the Arabic passage where Juwayni states that power is not an act of the servant but his attribute, created by Allah.
Notice the distinction between 'act' and 'attribute'.
2
Understand the confusion about Ash'ari's view
The passage quotes al-Dajani about a famous saying attributed to al-Ash'ari that seems to deny kasb. See how Juwayni clarifies that this is a misunderstanding.
The phrase 'no acquisition is obtained from it' is controversial.
3
Explore the proof that power exists before the act
Juwayni explains that the power of the servant is a force existing in his limbs before the action, dependent on sound causes. Denying this is obstinacy.
4
Reflect on the analogy from plants and minerals
Juwayni uses the example of forces in plants and minerals that chemists extract to argue that human power is similarly real and pre-existing.
This shows that denying pre-existing power contradicts observable reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتعالى تقديرا وخلقا . فإن وقع يفعل الله تبارك وتعالى وهو القدرة ، وليست القدرة فعلا للعبد ، وإنما هي صفته ، وهي ملك الله تبارك وتعالى وخلق الله ، وإذا كان موقع الفعل خلقا الله ، فالواقع به مضاف خلقة الرب خلق تبارك وتعالى . وتقدير . ويقول المحقق الدجاني عن القول المشهور والمعزو إلى الأشعرى فى كتب المتأخرين : « وأما ما قاله الفاهمون من كلام الأشيعرى فلا يتحصل به کسب ، وأن سموه کیا » ا هـ والناس فى فهم كلام الأشعرى فى قدرة العبد مضطربون ... والحق : أن القدرة المستجمعة لشرائط التأثير التى اثبتها الأشعرى .... و قال : أنها مع الفصل لا تتحقق الا عند تعلق قدرته تعالى بالفعل . وهو لا ينكر أن للعيد قدرة موجودة فيه قبل الفعل ، اذ قدرة العبد عبارة عن القوة المنبثة فى اعضائها المعين عنها بسلامة الأسباب والآلات ، وهي متحققة قبل الفعل ، بلا شبهة عند الجميع . فانكار. ذلك يكون مكابرة كما حققه المحقق ) عبد الحكيم ( في حاشيته على » المقدمات الأربع » الصدر الشريعة - فلتراجع - وليس الانسان باحط منزلة من النبات والمعدن المودعة فيهما قوى يستخلصهما الكيماويون ، و يبرزونها تحت نظر الناظرين ، وكم للمبدع الحكيم من قوى أودعها في الكون لا يعلو ادراكها على أحيط الناس عقولا ، فيكون الكلام مع من ينكر ذلك ضائعا . ومعنى تعلق قدرة الله وارادته بفعل العبد: اقداره للفيد على المضى فى مقتضى قدرته وارادته : قال الأستاذ الامام ا أبو منصور عبد القاهر التميمى » فى « الفرق بين الفرق » (٩٤) ) وان الله تعالى اذا علم حدوث شيء من أفعال العباد ولم يمنع منه فقـ اراد حدوثه ، وهو الحق . أ . هـ (ز).
And Exalted in decree and creation. For if it occurs by the act of Allah Blessed and Exalted, and that is power (al-qudra), and power is not an act of the servant, but rather it is his attribute, and it is the property of Allah Blessed and Exalted and His creation. And if the locus of the action is the creation of Allah, then what occurs is added to the creation of the Lord, Exalted and Exalted. And decree (al-taqdir). And the investigator al-Dajani says about the famous saying attributed to al-Ash'ari in the books of the later scholars: 'As for what the understanders of al-Ash'ari's speech have said, no acquisition (kasb) is obtained from it, even if they call it kasb.' End quote. And people in understanding al-Ash'ari's speech concerning the power of the servant are in confusion. And the truth is that the power which gathers the conditions of effect which al-Ash'ari established... and he said that it, with the resolution, is not realized except when His power, Exalted, is connected to the act. And he does not deny that the servant has a power existing in him before the act, for the power of the servant is an expression of the force scattered in his limbs, aided by the soundness of causes and instruments, and it is realized before the act, without doubt according to all. So denying that is obstinacy, as verified by the investigator 'Abd al-Hakim in his gloss on 'The Four Premises' of al-Sadr al-Shari'a – so refer to it. And man is not lower in status than plants and minerals in which are deposited forces that chemists extract and display them before the eyes of observers. And how many forces the wise Originator has deposited in the universe whose perception the most intelligent of people cannot attain, so speaking with one who denies that is futile. And the meaning of the connection of Allah's power and will with the act of the servant: His enabling the servant to proceed according to the requirement of his power and will. Al-Ustadh al-Imam Abu Mansur 'Abd al-Qahir al-Tamimi said in 'The Difference Between the Sects' (94): 'And indeed Allah, Exalted, when He knows the occurrence of something from the acts of servants and does not prevent it, then He wills its occurrence, and that is the truth.' End quote.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a combined definition and proof concerning the nature of power (qudra) in the Ash'ari school. It begins by stating that the actual occurrence of an action is by Allah's act, and that power is not the servant's act but his attribute, created by Allah. Then it addresses a common confusion about al-Ash'ari's view: some later scholars quoted a statement that acquisition (kasb) cannot be obtained from his speech. The author clarifies that the correct view is that power exists in the servant before the action as a capacity distributed in his limbs, dependent on sound causes. Denying this is obstinacy, as even inanimate objects have forces. Then it explains the connection of divine power and will to the servant's act: it means Allah enables the servant to act according to his own power and will. The passage concludes with a quote from Abu Mansur 'Abd al-Qahir al-Tamimi affirming that when Allah knows an act and does not prevent it, He wills it.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudra)
الكسب (al-kasb)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Ash'ari view denies any real power in the servant before the act.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Ash'ari does not deny a real power; it exists as a created attribute before the act.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the nature of the power (qudra) in the servant?
A) It is an act of the servant.
B) It is an attribute of the servant created by Allah.
C) It is non-existent before the act.
D) It is identical to divine power.

Key Takeaway
Human power is a real created attribute existing before action, not a product of human will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you truly feel that your ability to do it was a borrowed gift from Allah? How would your repentance change if you internalized that your power to obey also comes from Him every moment?
?
Juwayni says denying the servant's power before the act is 'obstinacy.' Is there an area in your life where you are stubbornly claiming your abilities as your own, forgetting they are created and sustained by Allah? What would surrender look like practically today?
?
The passage compares human power to forces in plants and minerals that are extracted by chemists. If your very capacity to act is a force deposited by Allah, what response does that demand from you in your next act of worship? Not just knowledge, but actual heartfelt gratitude.

The Meaning of Divine Connection to Human Action
Juwayni explains the meaning of divine connection to human action as enabling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari interpretation of how Allah's power and will relate to human actions: through enabling the servant to act according to his own power and will.

Core Idea
Divine enabling makes human action real without compromising God's sovereignty.

Having established that human power is a created attribute, we now ask: how does this power relate to God's power? In this passage, Juwayni defines the term 'talluq' (connection) and clarifies that it means Allah enables the servant to proceed with his action. A quote from al-Tamimi reinforces that God's knowledge and non-prevention imply His will. This resolves the tension between predestination and human agency.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of 'talluq'
Read the Arabic where Juwayni says: 'And the meaning of the connection of Allah's power and will with the act of the servant: His enabling the servant to proceed according to the requirement of his power and will.'
The key term is 'iqdar' (enabling).
2
Understand the concept of enabling
Juwayni explains that the connection does not mean God directly does the act, but that He enables the servant, i.e., creates the power and allows its exercise.
3
Analyze the quote from al-Tamimi
The quote states that when Allah knows an act and does not prevent it, He wills it. This affirms that divine will accompanies human actions without coercion.
This is a classical Ash'ari position.
4
Reflect on the synthesis
Consider how this view balances divine sovereignty and human accountability: all power comes from Allah, but the servant's choice and action are real within that framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتعالى تقديرا وخلقا . فإن وقع يفعل الله تبارك وتعالى وهو القدرة ، وليست القدرة فعلا للعبد ، وإنما هي صفته ، وهي ملك الله تبارك وتعالى وخلق الله ، وإذا كان موقع الفعل خلقا الله ، فالواقع به مضاف خلقة الرب خلق تبارك وتعالى . وتقدير . ويقول المحقق الدجاني عن القول المشهور والمعزو إلى الأشعرى فى كتب المتأخرين : « وأما ما قاله الفاهمون من كلام الأشيعرى فلا يتحصل به کسب ، وأن سموه کیا » ا هـ والناس فى فهم كلام الأشعرى فى قدرة العبد مضطربون ... والحق : أن القدرة المستجمعة لشرائط التأثير التى اثبتها الأشعرى .... و قال : أنها مع الفصل لا تتحقق الا عند تعلق قدرته تعالى بالفعل . وهو لا ينكر أن للعيد قدرة موجودة فيه قبل الفعل ، اذ قدرة العبد عبارة عن القوة المنبثة فى اعضائها المعين عنها بسلامة الأسباب والآلات ، وهي متحققة قبل الفعل ، بلا شبهة عند الجميع . فانكار. ذلك يكون مكابرة كما حققه المحقق ) عبد الحكيم ( في حاشيته على » المقدمات الأربع » الصدر الشريعة - فلتراجع - وليس الانسان باحط منزلة من النبات والمعدن المودعة فيهما قوى يستخلصهما الكيماويون ، و يبرزونها تحت نظر الناظرين ، وكم للمبدع الحكيم من قوى أودعها في الكون لا يعلو ادراكها على أحيط الناس عقولا ، فيكون الكلام مع من ينكر ذلك ضائعا . ومعنى تعلق قدرة الله وارادته بفعل العبد: اقداره للفيد على المضى فى مقتضى قدرته وارادته : قال الأستاذ الامام ا أبو منصور عبد القاهر التميمى » فى « الفرق بين الفرق » (٩٤) ) وان الله تعالى اذا علم حدوث شيء من أفعال العباد ولم يمنع منه فقـ اراد حدوثه ، وهو الحق . أ . هـ (ز).
And Exalted in decree and creation. For if it occurs by the act of Allah Blessed and Exalted, and that is power (al-qudra), and power is not an act of the servant, but rather it is his attribute, and it is the property of Allah Blessed and Exalted and His creation. And if the locus of the action is the creation of Allah, then what occurs is added to the creation of the Lord, Exalted and Exalted. And decree (al-taqdir). And the investigator al-Dajani says about the famous saying attributed to al-Ash'ari in the books of the later scholars: 'As for what the understanders of al-Ash'ari's speech have said, no acquisition (kasb) is obtained from it, even if they call it kasb.' End quote. And people in understanding al-Ash'ari's speech concerning the power of the servant are in confusion. And the truth is that the power which gathers the conditions of effect which al-Ash'ari established... and he said that it, with the resolution, is not realized except when His power, Exalted, is connected to the act. And he does not deny that the servant has a power existing in him before the act, for the power of the servant is an expression of the force scattered in his limbs, aided by the soundness of causes and instruments, and it is realized before the act, without doubt according to all. So denying that is obstinacy, as verified by the investigator 'Abd al-Hakim in his gloss on 'The Four Premises' of al-Sadr al-Shari'a – so refer to it. And man is not lower in status than plants and minerals in which are deposited forces that chemists extract and display them before the eyes of observers. And how many forces the wise Originator has deposited in the universe whose perception the most intelligent of people cannot attain, so speaking with one who denies that is futile. And the meaning of the connection of Allah's power and will with the act of the servant: His enabling the servant to proceed according to the requirement of his power and will. Al-Ustadh al-Imam Abu Mansur 'Abd al-Qahir al-Tamimi said in 'The Difference Between the Sects' (94): 'And indeed Allah, Exalted, when He knows the occurrence of something from the acts of servants and does not prevent it, then He wills its occurrence, and that is the truth.' End quote.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a combined definition and proof concerning the nature of power (qudra) in the Ash'ari school. It begins by stating that the actual occurrence of an action is by Allah's act, and that power is not the servant's act but his attribute, created by Allah. Then it addresses a common confusion about al-Ash'ari's view: some later scholars quoted a statement that acquisition (kasb) cannot be obtained from his speech. The author clarifies that the correct view is that power exists in the servant before the action as a capacity distributed in his limbs, dependent on sound causes. Denying this is obstinacy, as even inanimate objects have forces. Then it explains the connection of divine power and will to the servant's act: it means Allah enables the servant to act according to his own power and will. The passage concludes with a quote from Abu Mansur 'Abd al-Qahir al-Tamimi affirming that when Allah knows an act and does not prevent it, He wills it.

Key Terms
التعلق (al-ta'allaq)
الإقدار (al-iqdar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God wills an action, He directly creates it, eliminating human power.
Correction: The passage clarifies that divine will works through enabling the servant's own power, not by replacing it.

Checkpoint
What does the passage mean by 'the connection of Allah's power and will with the act of the servant'?
A) Allah directly creates the act.
B) Allah enables the servant to act according to his own power.
C) Allah's power replaces the servant's power.
D) The servant acts independently of Allah's will.

Key Takeaway
Divine connection to human action means Allah enables the servant to act with his own power, not that He performs the act directly.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your ability to act is entirely from Allah's enabling, why do you often feel proud of your own accomplishments as if you achieved them alone? Will you today thank Allah specifically for granting you the power to do even a small good deed?
?
When you commit a sin, and Allah did not prevent you, does that mean He is pleased with it? How does this lesson change the way you view your failures and your need for His mercy?

Divine Decree
intermediate

Sunni Doctrine of Qadar: Human Choice Under Divine Decree
Juwayni expounds Sunni qadar doctrine and refutes Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sunni theology affirms both divine decree and human choice, refuting the Qadariyya claim of independent human creation.

Core Idea
Human acts are real but ultimately dependent on Allah's decree and power.

In this passage, Imam al-Juwayni clarifies the Sunni position on qadar (divine decree) by distinguishing it from the Qadariyya sect, who claimed that humans create their own acts independently. He explains how Allah grants choice and power, while remaining the ultimate Creator and Ordainer of all actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key claim of the Qadariyya
Read the passage to find what the misguided sect claimed about creation and invention. Notice how Juwayni refutes them by affirming Allah's sole creativity.
The Qadariyya claimed 'استبدادا بالاختراع' – monopolizing invention.
2
Understand the Sunni explanation of power and choice
Examine how Juwayni describes the relationship between Allah's decree, the power He creates in the servant, and the servant's choice (ikhtiyar). Note the sequence: Allah creates power, prepares causes, creates motives, and knows the outcome.
3
Grasp the dual attribution of the act
Notice that the act is attributed both to the servant (as acquirer) and to Allah (as Creator). The servant is described as a 'free agent' (فاعل مختار) yet his act is 'the decree of Allah, willed by Him, a created decreed thing.'
This avoids both compulsion and independence.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Read the final sentence: the servant is commanded, prohibited, and rebuked. This shows moral accountability despite divine decree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ملك الله العبد اختيارا يصرف به القدرة . واذا وقع بالقدرة شيئا الى الواقع الى حكم الله ، من حيث أنه وقع بفعل الله تعالى ، ولو اهتدت لهذا الفرقة الضالة لما كان بيننا وبينهم خلاف ، ولكنهم أدعوا : استبدادا بالاختراع وانفرادا بالخلق والابتداع ، فضلوا وأضلوا ، ونبين تميزنا عنهم بتفريع المذهبين .. فانا لما أضفنا فعل العبد الى تقدير الآله . قلنا : أحدث الله تبارك وتعالى القدر في العبد على أقدار أحاط بها عليه ، وهيا أسباب الفعل وسلب الله العلم بالتفاصيل ، وأراد من العبد أن يفعل فأحدث فيه دواعي مستحثة وخيرة وارادة ، وعلم أن الأفعال ستقع على قدر معلوم ، فوقعت بالقدرة التي اخترعها للعبد على ما علم وأراد . وللعباد اختيارهم واتصافهم بالاقتدار، والقدرة خلق الله ابتداء ، ومقدورها مضاف اليه مشيئة وعلما وقضاء وخلقا وبقاء ، من حيث أنه نتيجة ما انفرد بخلقه، وهو القدرة ولو لم يرد وقوع مقدوره لما أقدره عليه ، ولما هيا أسباب وقوعه . ومن هدى لهذا ، استمر له الحق المبين ، فالعيد فاعل مختار مطالب مأمور منهى ، وفعله تقدير الله ، مراد له ، وخلق مقضى . ونحن نضرب اليه الناظر في ذلك فنقول : فى ذلك مثلا شرعيا يستروح . العبد لا يملك أن يتصرف في مال سيده ، ولو استبد بالتصرف فيه ، لم ينفذ تصرفه ، فاذا أذن له فى بيع ماله فباعه نفذ ، والبيع في التحقيق معزى الى السيد ، من حيث ان سببه اذنه . ولولا أذنه ينفذ التصرف . ولكن للعبد يؤمر بالتصرف وينهى ويوبخ على المخالفة
And Allah has given the servant choice (ikhtiyar) by which he directs the power. And when something occurs by power to the reality by the judgment of Allah, in that it occurs by the act of Allah, Exalted. And if this misguided sect had been guided to this, there would have been no disagreement between us and them. But they claimed: monopolizing invention and being alone in creation and origination, so they went astray and led astray. And we explain our distinction from them by the branching of the two schools. For when we attributed the act of the servant to the decree of God, we said: Allah Blessed and Exalted created the power in the servant according to decrees which He encompassed upon him, and He prepared the causes of the act, and Allah removed knowledge of the details, and He willed from the servant that he act, so He created in him stimulating motives and choice and will, and He knew that the acts would occur according to a known measure, so they occurred by the power which He invented for the servant according to what He knew and willed. And the servants have their choice and their description with capability, and power is the creation of Allah initially, and its object is added to Him in will, knowledge, decree, creation, and permanence, in that it is the result of what He alone created, which is power. And had He not willed the occurrence of its object, He would not have empowered him over it, and He would not have prepared the causes of its occurrence. And whoever is guided to this, clear truth continues for him. So the servant is a free agent, required, commanded, prohibited, and his act is the decree of Allah, willed by Him, and a created decreed thing. And we strike toward the one who looks into that, and we say: in that a legal analogy by which one finds ease. The servant does not have the right to dispose of his master's property, and if he acts independently in disposing of it, his disposal is not executed. So if he permits him to sell his property and he sells it, it is executed, and the sale in reality is attributed to the master, in that its cause is his permission. And were it not for his permission, the disposal would not be executed. But the servant is commanded to dispose and is forbidden and rebuked for violating.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition and refutation. It first states that Allah has given the servant a free choice (ikhtiyar) to direct his power. The misguided sect (the Qadariyya) claimed that the servant creates his own acts independently. The Sunnis distinguish themselves by affirming that the act is added to Allah's decree: Allah creates the power in the servant according to His decrees, prepares causes, creates motives and will, and the act occurs by the power He invented. The servant's choice and capability are real, but power is Allah's creation and its effect is attributed to Him in all aspects. The passage then offers a legal analogy: a servant cannot dispose of his master's property without permission. If the master permits a sale, the sale is attributed to the master because of his permission, yet the servant is commanded, forbidden, and rebuked. Similarly, human acts are attributed to Allah as Creator and to the servant as acquirer, with real choice and accountability.

Key Terms
الاختيار (al-ikhtiyar)
التقدير (al-taqdir)
القدرة (al-qudra)
الفرقة الضالة (al-firqa al-dalla)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, how does a human act occur?
A) The human creates his own act independently.
B) Allah creates the act directly without human involvement.
C) Allah creates power and motives in the human, and the human acts by that power while Allah decrees all.
D) The human has no role; Allah does everything.

Key Takeaway
Human acts are real and willed by Allah, with the servant as a free agent responsible for his choices, while Allah remains the sole Creator of power and decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says Allah 'removed knowledge of the details' from you. How does this affect your trust in Allah's wisdom when you cannot see the full picture of your trials and choices? Are you willing to submit to His decree even when you don't understand it?
?
Juwayni states that the servant is 'a free agent, required, commanded, prohibited.' You cannot deny your choices, yet they are decreed. Does this make you more accountable or less? How will you change your approach to obeying commands knowing that your act is ultimately created by Allah but chosen by you?
?
The Qadariyya went astray by claiming independence in creation. In what areas of your life do you subtly act as if you are the sole creator of your success or failure, forgetting Allah's power and will? What step will you take today to realign your heart with tawheed in your daily actions?

Divine Decree

The Legal Analogy: Divine Permission and Human Agency
Juwayni uses a legal analogy to illustrate divine decree and human agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the master-servant legal analogy illustrates the relationship between divine decree and human action, showing that human acts are real but dependent on Allah's permission.

Core Idea
Like a servant acting by his master's permission, humans act by Allah's decree and are accountable.

Imam al-Juwayni now presents a concrete legal analogy to make the abstract doctrine of qadar accessible. He compares the relationship between Allah and humans to that of a master and his servant, where the servant can only act within the master's permission. This analogy clarifies how human acts are both real and attributed to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy carefully
Read the passage about the servant and the master. Identify the key elements: the servant's inability to dispose of the master's property without permission, the effect of permission, and the attribution of the sale.
The analogy is 'المثل الشرعي' – a legal analogy meant to provide ease (يستروح).
2
Analyze the attribution of the act
Notice that the sale, when performed with permission, is attributed to the master 'in reality' (في التحقيق) because its cause is the master's permission. Yet the servant is the one who performs the sale.
This mirrors the human act: attributed to Allah as Creator, to the human as acquirer.
3
Observe the consequences for the servant
The servant is commanded, forbidden, and rebuked for violating. This shows that despite the attribution to the master, the servant has real agency and accountability.
The analogy preserves moral responsibility.
4
Connect to the doctrine
Reflect on how this analogy helps explain the earlier doctrinal points: human choice is real, acts are decreed, and accountability remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

To whom is the sale attributed 'in reality' in Juwayni's analogy?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

The Ash'ari Doctrine of Kasb: Human Agency and Divine Creation
Juwayni explains the Ash'ari mechanism of kasb and human agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Juwayni's doctrine of kasb affirms genuine human choice while attributing all effective power and creation to God.

Core Idea
Human action is real but created by God; we acquire it by choice.

Juwayni begins by establishing that God has granted humans a genuine choice (ikhtiyār) through which they direct the power (qudra) that God creates in them. He contrasts this with the Mu'tazilite claim of independent human creation, then details how God creates the capacity, motives, and will for the act while still holding humans accountable.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Notice Juwayni's contrast between the Ash'ari view and the misguided sect (Mu'tazila).
The passage is dense; focus on the sequence of divine acts.
2
Identify the two schools
Juwayni says the misguided sect claimed exclusive invention and sole creation. Identify what the Ash'aris affirm instead: that God creates power, prepares causes, and denies detailed knowledge.
3
Trace the mechanism of kasb
Follow the steps: God creates capacity, prepares causes, creates motives and will, and the act occurs by the power He created. Note that the servant's choice is real.
Use the guided breakdown below to see each step.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Juwayni concludes that the servant is an agent, choosing, commanded, forbidden. Understand that this preserves human responsibility while affirming divine causality.
This resolves the apparent tension between predestination and free will.

وقد ملك الله العبد اختيارا يصرف به القدرة. وإذا وقع بالقدرة شيء إلى الواقع إلى حكم الله، من حيث أنه وقع بفعل الله تعالى، ولو اهتدت لهذا الفرقة الضالة لما كان بيننا وبينهم خلاف، ولكنهم ادعوا: استبدادا بالاختراع وانفرادا بالخلق والابتداع، فضلوا وأضلوا، ونبين تميزنا عنهم بتفريع المذهبين.. فإنا لما أضفنا فعل العبد إلى تقدير الآله. قلنا: أحدث الله تبارك وتعالى القدر في العبد على أقدار أحاط بها عليه، وهيأ أسباب الفعل وسلب الله العلم بالتفاصيل، وأراد من العبد أن يفعل فأحدث فيه دواعي مستحثة (١) وخيرة وإرادة، وعلم أن الأفعال ستقع على قدر معلوم، فوقعت بالقدرة التي اخترعها للعبد على ما علم وأراد. وللعباد اختيارهم واتصافهم بالاقتدار، والقدرة خلق الله ابتداء، ومقدورها مضاف إليه مشيئة وعلما وقضاء وخلقا وبقاء، من حيث أنه نتيجة ما انفرد بخلقه، وهو القدرة ولو لم يرد وقوع مقدوره لما أقدره عليه (٢)، ولما هيأ أسباب وقوعه. ومن هدي لهذا، استمر له الحق المبين، فالعبد فاعل مختار مطالب مأمور منهي، وفعله تقدير الله، مراد له، وخلق مقضي. ونحن نضرب للناظر في ذلك مثلا شرعيا يستروح به: العبد لا يملك أن يتصرف في مال سيده، ولو استبد بالتصرف فيه، لم ينفذ تصرفه، فإذا أذن له في بيع ماله فباعه نفذ، والبيع في التحقيق معزى إلى السيد، من حيث أن سببه إذنه. ولولا إذنه لا ينفذ التصرف. ولكن العبد يؤمر بالتصرف وينهى ويوبخ على المخالفة ويعاقب، فهذا - والله - الحق الذي لا غطاء دونه، ولا مراء فيه لمن وعاه حق وعيه، ولا يكابر فيه
And God has given the servant a choice by which he directs the power. And when something occurs by power according to God's decree, insofar as it occurs by the act of God Almighty—and if this misguided sect had been guided to this, there would have been no dispute between us and them, but they claimed exclusive invention and sole creation and origination, so they went astray and led others astray. And we clarify our distinction from them by differentiating the two schools. For when we attribute the servant's act to God's decree, we say: God, blessed and exalted, created capacity in the servant according to capacities He encompassed for him, and prepared the causes of the act, and God denied knowledge of details, and willed from the servant that he act, so He created in him inciting motives (1) and choice and will, and He knew that the acts would occur according to a known measure, so they occurred by the power which He invented for the servant according to what He knew and willed. And the servants have their choice and their description of capability, and power is God's creation initially, and its object is attributed to His will, knowledge, decree, creation, and preservation, insofar as it is a result of what He uniquely created, namely power. And had He not willed the occurrence of its object, He would not have empowered him over it (2), nor prepared the causes of its occurrence. And whoever is guided to this, clear truth continues for him. So the servant is an agent, choosing, demanded, commanded, forbidden; his act is God's decree, willed by Him, and created and decreed. And we strike for the observer in that a legal example to be refreshed by: the servant does not own the right to dispose of his master's property, and if he acts independently in disposing of it, his disposal is not effective. If the master gives him permission to sell his property and he sells, it is effective, and the sale in reality is attributed to the master, because its cause is his permission. Without his permission, the disposal is not effective. But the servant is commanded to dispose, prohibited, rebuked for opposition, and punished. This—by God—is the truth behind which there is no cover, nor any dispute for one who understands it rightly and does not obstinately dispute it.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is an argumentative exposition of the Ash'ari position on human action (kasb) against the Mu'tazila. Juwayni first states that God has given the human a choice (ikhtiyār) by which he directs his power (qudra). He then contrasts the Ash'ari view with that of the 'misguided sect' (the Mu'tazila) who claim that humans create their own acts independently. Juwayni clarifies that when Ash'aris attribute the servant's act to God's decree, they mean that God creates capacity (qudra) in the servant according to a predetermined measure, prepares the causes of the act, but withholds detailed knowledge from the human. God wills the act, so He creates inciting motives (dawā'ī mustaḥaththa) and choice (khiyara) and will (irāda) in the servant. God knows the acts will occur as determined, and they occur by the power He created in the servant according to His knowledge and will. Juwayni emphasizes that the servant indeed has choice and capability, but that power is God's creation from the beginning, and its object is attributed to God's will, knowledge, decree, creation, and preservation. If God did not will the act, He would not have empowered the human or prepared its causes. Then Juwayni presents a legal analogy: a servant (slave) does not own his master's property; if he acts independently, his action is void. But if the master gives permission, the sale is effective and attributed to the master, while the servant is commanded, prohibited, rebuked, and punished. Similarly, human acts are effective by God's permission but are the human's acquisition (kasb) and thus subject to command and consequence. Juwayni concludes that this is the clear truth.

Key Terms
الاختيار (choice)
القدرة (power)
التقدير (decree)
الأسباب (causes)
الدواعي (motives)
الارادة (will)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash'ari doctrine of kasb denies any real human agency or choice.
Correction: Juwayni explicitly states that the servant has choice (ikhtiyār) and is an agent (fā'il), commanded and forbidden. Human action is real, though created by God.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what does God create in the servant to direct the act?
A) The act itself directly
B) Choice (ikhtiyār) and motives (dawā'ī) and will
C) The power to create independently
D) The desire to sin

Key Takeaway
Humans have real choice and are accountable, but all effective power and creation belong to God; the act is a divine creation acquired by human choice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever blame God's decree to avoid feeling guilty? After reading this, how does knowing that your choice is real and created by God change your sense of accountability?
?
If every good act you do is ultimately created by God, does that make you feel less proud or more grateful? How does this affect the way you pray for strength to do good?
?
Juwayni says God gives you a choice and then judges you for it. Can you still think God is unfair when you fail? What would you say to Him if He asked you about a sin you committed, knowing He gave you the power and the choice?

Divine Decree
intermediate

The Slave Analogy: Human Action as Acquisition by Permission
Juwayni uses a legal analogy to clarify kasb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's legal analogy of the slave and master, which illustrates how human actions are real acquisitions (kasb) effective by God's permission yet subject to command and consequence.

Core Idea
Our actions are like a slave's sale: effective only by the Master's permission, yet we are accountable.

Juwayni provides a clear legal analogy to make the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb accessible. A slave cannot dispose of his master's property independently; only with explicit permission does his action become effective and attributable to the master. Similarly, human actions are real and effective only by God's permission and creative power, yet humans are commanded, rebuked, and punished for them.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy
Read the Arabic text of the analogy and its translation. Focus on the two scenarios: without permission and with permission.
Juwayni presents this as a 'legal example' to refresh the mind.
2
Identify the key elements
Identify the roles: slave (human), master (God), property (acts), permission (divine will and creation), sale (the act).
The sale is effective only because of the master's permission.
3
Understand the attribution
Juwayni says the sale is in reality attributed to the master because its cause is his permission. Similarly, human acts are attributed to God as ultimate cause.
This does not negate the slave's role as the one who performs the sale.
4
Apply the analogy to human responsibility
The slave is commanded, prohibited, rebuked, and punished despite the act being attributed to the master. So humans are accountable for their acquisitions.
This resolves the problem of how God can command and judge if He creates all actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni's analogy, why is the slave's sale effective when the master gives permission?
A) Because the slave owns the property
B) Because the sale is attributed to the master due to his permission
C) Because the slave creates the sale independently
D) Because the master directly performs the sale

Key Takeaway
Human actions are like a slave's sale with the master's permission: real and effective, attributable to God as cause, yet the basis for divine command and judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life do you act as if you are the independent ‘master’ of your actions, forgetting that every effective action is only by His permission? Will you consciously attribute your next success to Him alone?
?
If the slave is punished for disobeying the master despite the master being the ultimate cause, how does this truth reframe your view of personal accountability before God? Will you take full responsibility for your sins today?
?
The master’s permission does not remove the slave’s duty to obey commands. Which command of God do you know to be true but have been excusing by saying ‘only God can change my heart’? How will you respond as if His permission is already granted for you to act?

Juwayni's Refutation of the Objection Against Divine Sealing
Juwayni answers the objection that sealing verses imply compulsion, affirming obligation remains.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's sealing of hearts does not negate human moral responsibility and how Juwayni refutes the objection using rational analogy.

Core Idea
Divine sealing does not cancel obligation; commanding while preventing is absurd.

This passage presents an objection raised against the Ash'ari position on God's sealing of hearts: if God seals, how can He hold people accountable? Juwayni responds by clarifying that those sealed were still addressed with commands and possessed ability. He then refutes the mistaken view that sealing implies compulsion, using a powerful analogy to expose its absurdity. This lesson walks through the objection, Juwayni's answer, and his final critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the objection
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the objector's claim: that verses about sealing suggest God leads people to misguidance. This is the challenge Juwayni must answer.
The objection targets divine justice and human responsibility.
2
Understand Juwayni's first answer: obligation remains
Juwayni states that those sealed were still obligated with faith and Islam, described as having ability and power. He then introduces the mistaken view that they were forced, and refutes it.
The principle: sealing does not remove moral duty.
3
Analyze the analogy and the distinction
Juwayni uses the analogy of a tied man thrown into sea told not to get wet to show the absurdity of commanding while preventing. He further distinguishes God's creative command (e.g., 'Be apes') from legislative command (obligation), which the objector conflates.
This clarifies the rational necessity of distinguishing God's actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان قيل : على ما تحملون آيات الطبع والختم والاضلال في القرآن . وهى متضمنة الرب تعالى الاشقياء الى ضلالتهم ؟ قلنا : اذا أتاح الله تعالى حل هذا الاشكال ، والجواب على هذا السؤال لم يبق على ذوي البصائر بعده غموض . فنقول أولا : من أنبأ الله تعالى عن الطبع على قلوبهم كانوا مخاطبين بالايمان ، مطالبين الاسلام ، والتزام الاحكام ، مطالبة تكليف ودعاء ، مع وصفهم بالتمكن والاقتدار والايثار كما سبق تقريره في صدر الفصل اعتقد أنهم كانوا ممنوعين مأمورين مصدودين قهرا ، ومدعوين ، فالتكليف اذن عنده بمثابة ما لو شد من الرجل يداه ورجلاه رباطا ، وألقى فى البحر ، ثم قيل له : لا تبتل . وهذا منتهى لا يحمل دائع الرسل عليه الا عابت بنفسه مجترى على ربه ، ولا فرق عند هذا القائل بين أمر التسخير والتكوين في قوله تعالى : « كونوا قردة خاسئين » وقوله تبارك وتعالى : « أن يقول له كن فيكون » وبين أمر التكليف .. نعوذ بالله من الركون الى كل ما ينطق به اللسان من غير مباحثة عن أسرار المعقولات .
If it is said: 'How do you interpret the verses of sealing, covering, and misguidance in the Qur’an, which imply that God – exalted is He – leads the wretched to their misguidance?' We say: 'If God facilitates solving this difficulty, and the answer to this question, no ambiguity remains after it for those of insight. So we say first: Those whom God informed about the sealing upon their hearts were addressed with faith, required with Islam, and obligated to abide by the rulings, with the requirement of obligation and invitation, while they are described as having ability, power, and preference – as previously established in the opening of the chapter. The one who believes that they were prevented, commanded, forcibly repelled, and invited – then obligation in his view is like if a man’s hands and legs were tied with a rope, and he was thrown into the sea, then it was said to him: “Do not get wet.” This is the utmost that does not carry the pillars of the messengers except by one who slanders himself and is insolent towards his Lord. And there is no difference in this person’s view between the command of subjugation and creation in His statement “Be apes, despised” and His statement “He says to it ‘Be’ and it is” and the command of obligation. We seek refuge in God from leaning towards everything that the tongue utters without investigating the secrets of rational matters.'
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer format typical of kalam. The objector asks: If God seals hearts, how can you hold people accountable? Juwayni begins by affirming that the answer is clear to the insightful. He then states the key principle: those whom God declared sealed were still addressed with commands of faith and Islam, described as having ability and choice. Then he refutes a mistaken alternative view: that the sealed were prevented and forced while still being commanded – a contradiction. He illustrates this absurdity with an analogy: tying a man and throwing him into the sea then telling him not to get wet. This, he says, would never be attributed to the messengers. He further argues that this mistaken view conflates God's creative commands (like 'Be apes' and 'Be') with legislative commands (obligation), which is an error. The passage ends with a prayer for protection from speaking without rational investigation.

Key Terms
طبع
ختم
إضلال
تكليف
تسخير
تكوين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's sealing of hearts removes all moral responsibility and makes it unjust to hold people accountable.
Correction: Sealing does not negate obligation; the sealed still possess ability and choice, and are commanded. Juwayni shows the absurdity of commanding while preventing using the analogy of a tied man thrown into the sea.

Checkpoint
What analogy does Juwayni use to illustrate the absurdity of commanding someone while preventing them?
A) A man tied and thrown into the sea told not to get wet
B) A bird in a cage told to fly
C) A child told to be quiet while sleeping
D) A blind man told to see

Key Takeaway
Juwayni shows that divine sealing does not nullify obligation, and conflating God's creative command with His legislative command is a grave rational error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used your perceived weaknesses or circumstances as an excuse to avoid obeying a clear command of Allah? How does Juwayni's analogy of the tied man challenge that excuse?
?
When you read verses about Allah sealing hearts, does your heart tremble with fear that you might be among those sealed, or do you assume it only applies to others? What would change in your prayers if you genuinely believed your heart's condition is in Allah's hands yet you are still fully accountable?
?
Juwayni warns against speaking about Allah without rational investigation. In what areas of your own practice have you accepted teachings about qadar without examining whether they align with the balance of divine sovereignty and human responsibility? What is one step you can take this week to rectify that?

Divine Sealing as Facilitation of Good and Evil
Juwayni explains sealing as God's facilitation of good for believers and evil for disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's positive explanation of divine sealing as God's facilitation of good for believers and evil for disbelievers, and how this differs from deterministic interpretations.

Core Idea
Divine sealing is God's facilitation of good or evil, not arbitrary compulsion.

Juwayni now provides the correct interpretation of the Qur'anic terms 'sealing', 'covering', and 'veils'. He rejects the erroneous views of other sects and explains that these terms refer to God's active facilitation: for those He wills good, He perfects intellect and removes obstacles; for those He wills evil, He distances good and allows desires to dominate. This is all by God's decree, but it is a consequence of human choice, not compulsion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the two parallel scenarios presented by Juwayni.
Pay attention to the verbs: أكمل, صرف, أزاح, وفق, سهل, قطع, قبض for good, and قدر, هيأ, حبب, عرض for evil.
2
Identify the two scenarios
Find where Juwayni describes God's action for the one He wills good and for the one He wills evil. Note the sequence of facilitations in each case.
3
Reflect on the theme of facilitation
Consider how Juwayni's explanation avoids the error of compulsion: sealing is a result of God's facilitation of means, not direct causation of disbelief.
Juwayni emphasizes that this happens 'by God's decree and measure' (بقضاء الله وقدره).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا بطل ذلك فالوجه فى الكلام على هذه الآى ، وقد غوى في معانيها أكثر الفرق أن نقول : اذا أراد الله بعبد خيرا أكمل عقله ، وأتم بصيرته ، ثم صرف عنه العوائق والدوافع ، وأزاح عنه الموانع ، ووفق له قرناء الخير ، وسهل له سبيله ، وقطع عنه الملهيات ، وأسباب الغفلات والذهول ، وقبض له ما يقرب الى القربات فيوافيها ، ثم يعتادها ، ويمرن عليها . واذا أراد بعبد شرا ، قدر له ما يبعده عن الخير ويقضيه ، وهيأ له تماديه في الغى . وحبب اليه التشوف الى الشهوات ، وعرضه للآفات ، وكلما غلبت دواعى الشر ، خنست دواعي الخير ، ثم يستمر على الشرور ، على مر الدهور ، هاويا في مهاويها ، وتتعاون عليه الوساوس ونزعات الشيطان ، ونزوات النفس الأمارة بالسوء فتنشىء الغفلة غشاوة على قلبه ، بقضاء الله تبارك وتعالى وقدره ، فذلكم الطبع عافاكم الله والختم والأكنة .
And when that is invalidated, the correct approach regarding these verses – while most sects have erred in their meanings – is that we say: When God desires good for a servant, He perfects his intellect, completes his insight, then averts from him obstacles and deterrents, removes barriers, grants him good companions, eases his path, cuts off from him distractions and causes of heedlessness and forgetfulness, and draws near to him what brings him close to acts of devotion so that he attends to them, then becomes accustomed to them, and practices them. And when He desires evil for a servant, He decrees for him what distances him from good and brings it about, and prepares for him persistence in error. He makes longing for desires beloved to him, exposes him to afflictions, and whenever the prompts of evil prevail, the prompts of good recede. Then he continues in evils over the course of ages, falling into their depths, and the whisperings and incitements of Satan and the impulses of the soul commanding evil cooperate against him, so heedlessness creates a covering over his heart, by the decree and measure of God, the Blessed and Exalted. That is the sealing – may God preserve you – and the covering and the veils.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a positive exposition of the meaning of 'sealing' (طبع), 'covering' (ختم), and 'veils' (أكنة) in the Qur'an. Juwayni first notes that most sects have erred in understanding these terms. He then provides the correct interpretation: when God wills good for a person, He facilitates the means of good – perfecting intellect, removing obstacles, providing good companions, and making devotion easy so that it becomes habitual. Conversely, when God wills evil for a person, He facilitates the means of evil – distancing from good, making desires attractive, allowing whispers and impulses to dominate until heedlessness covers the heart. This is all by God's decree and measure (قضاء وقدر). Juwayni emphasizes that this is not compulsion; rather, it is God's response to the servant's own choices, as the earlier context of ability and preference (التمكن والاقتدار والايثار) indicates. The culmination is that 'sealing' is the result of a person's persistent evil actions, aided by divine facilitation, not an arbitrary imposition.

Key Terms

ختم
أكنة
توفيق
خذلان
قضاء
قدر
تكامل العقل
بصيرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That divine sealing is an arbitrary act of God that forces disbelief, without any cause or process.
Correction: Juwayni shows that sealing is the result of a series of divine facilitations: when God wills evil, He facilitates the means of evil (e.g., making desires attractive, allowing whispers) until heedlessness covers the heart. It is not a direct creation of disbelief but a consequence of His decree working through means.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what does God do when He desires evil for a servant?
A) He forces him to commit sin
B) He seals his heart directly without cause
C) He facilitates the means of evil and allows heedlessness to cover his heart
D) He creates disbelief in him by compulsion

Key Takeaway
Juwayni explains that divine sealing is the outcome of God's facilitation of the means of good or evil according to His will, not a forced fate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your own spiritual journey, can you identify moments where God made good easy for you—clearing obstacles and granting good companions? How did you respond to His tawfiq? What does your response reveal about the state of your heart?
?
Consider a time when you felt distant from good, drawn to desires, and heedless. According to this lesson, that too is by God's decree and measure. Do you recognize your own choices that contributed to that state? What will you do today to reverse that trajectory before the sealing becomes permanent?
?
If divine sealing is the outcome of God's facilitation based on His desire for you, what does that tell you about the urgency of seeking His desire for good? Are you actively removing distractions and persevering in devotion, or are you cooperating with the means of evil? What concrete step will you take tonight to align with the path of tawfiq?

Allah's Decree for Evil and the Seal on Hearts
Juwayni describes the process of divine decree leading to the seal on the heart.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah's decree for evil operates through a sequence of divinely-ordained causes culminating in the seal on the heart.

Core Idea
Allah's decree for evil works through a chain of causes, not by force.

Imam Juwayni explains the mechanism of divine decree when Allah intends evil for a servant. He describes a series of steps: from distancing from good, to beautifying desires, to the cooperation of satanic whisperings, until heedlessness covers the heart. This passage shows that the 'seal' is the outcome of a process, not an arbitrary compulsion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the sequence of events Juwayni describes.
Notice the use of 'then' and 'so'.
2
Identify the stages of divine decree
List the stages Juwayni mentions: Allah decrees, prepares, makes desirous, exposes, evil motives prevail, good retreats, etc.
3
Connect to the seal concept
Juwayni concludes that these events constitute the seal, stamp, and covering. Understand that the seal is the end result of this process.
4
Reflect on human agency
Ask yourself: Does this description negate human choice? Juwayni implies the servant continues in evil 'over the course of ages', suggesting ongoing actions.
The seal is not a forced compulsion but a divinely-willed outcome.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا أراد بعبد شرا ، قدر له ما يبعده عن الخير ويقضيه ، وهيأ له تماديه في الغى . وحبب اليه التشوف الى الشهوات ، وعرضه للآفات، وكلما غلبت دواعى الشر ، خنست دواعي الخير ، ثم يستمر على الشرور ، على مر الدهور ، هاويا في مهاويها ، وتتعاون عليه الوساوس ونزعات الشيطان ، ونزوات النفس الأمارة بالسوء فتنشىء الغفلة غشاوة على قلبه ، بقضاء الله تبارك وتعالى وقدره (۱) ، فذلكم الطبع - عافاكم الله - والختم والأكنة . وأنا أضرب في ذلك مثلا فأقول
And when He intends evil for a servant, He decrees for him what distances him from good and brings it about, and prepares for him prolongation in error. And He makes desirous for him yearning towards lusts, and exposes him to afflictions. And whenever the motives of evil prevail, the motives of good retreat. Then he continues in evils over the course of ages, falling into their pitfalls. And together upon him cooperate whisperings and incitements of Satan and impulses of the commanding soul to evil, so heedlessness creates a covering over his heart, by the decree of Allah, Blessed and Exalted, and His determination (1). So that is the seal – may Allah grant you well-being – and the stamp and the covering. And I will give an example concerning that and say:
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a theological explanation of how Allah's decree (qadr) operates when He intends evil for a servant. The author, Imam Juwayni, enumerates a sequence of divinely-ordained causes: Allah decrees means that distance the servant from good, makes him persist in error, beautifies desires, exposes him to afflictions, and allows evil motives to overcome good motives. Then the servant continues in evil over time, and satanic whisperings and the commanding soul (al-nafs al-ammāra) cooperate with him, causing heedlessness (ghafla) to create a covering (ghishāwa) over his heart. Juwayni explicitly states that this whole process occurs by Allah's decree and determination. Then he identifies this constellation of effects as the 'seal' (tab'), 'stamp' (khatm), and 'covering' (akina) mentioned in the Quran. He adds that he will give an example (mathal) to clarify further. Note that the passage does not negate human choice; it describes how divine decree works through secondary causes that influence but do not eliminate human agency.

Key Terms

قضاء
طبع
ختم
أكنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The seal implies God forcibly compels disbelief.
Correction: Juwayni describes the seal as the outcome of a divinely-willed process that involves the servant's own choices and circumstances, not a forced compulsion.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what is the result when Allah intends evil for a servant?
A) The servant is forced to commit evil without any choice.
B) Allah distances him from good, beautifies desires, and heedlessness covers his heart.
C) The servant is left entirely to his own devices.
D) The servant immediately becomes a disbeliever.

Key Takeaway
The seal on the heart is the divinely-willed culmination of a chain of causes initiated when Allah intends evil for a servant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself persistently drawn to a particular sin, ask yourself: is this a sign that the motives of evil are prevailing in my heart? What concrete step can I take today to invite the motives of good to return?
?
Juwayni describes a process where every step is decreed by Allah, yet your own heedlessness and choices are part of that chain. How does this challenge the excuse, 'I can't change; it's my qadr'? What is one area of disobedience you have been excusing, and what will you do this week to break the chain?
?
The seal is placed after heedlessness creates a covering over the heart. Are you aware of any 'coverings' that have formed over your heart – things that once bothered you but no longer do? What would it cost you to remove that covering before it becomes a seal?
