The Fixed Term of Lifespan and Refutation of Innovation
Juwayni defines ajal as God's knowledge and refutes the claim that killing cuts short the term.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's definition of ajal as God's knowledge of the time of death and why the claim that killing cuts short the term is invalid.

Core Idea
The lifespan is exactly what God knows—no killer shortens it.

Juwayni addresses a key debate about predestination: does killing someone cut their lifespan short? He defines ajal as the time God knows an event will occur. This leads to a clear refutation of the innovators' claim. Let's read his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the formal opening and the objection-response structure.
2
Identify the innovator claim
Find where Juwayni states the innovator claim. Ask yourself: what do they believe about killing and lifespans?
The claim appears after 'فزعم زاعمون منهم'.
3
Follow the refutation
Trace how Juwayni defines ajal and uses two objections (قيل/قلنا) to show the claim is impossible.
The core logic: if God knows a death, that is the term; possibilities do not apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فى الأجال والارزاق
لكل حدوث وعدم، وبقاء وفناء، وحياة وممات: أجل معلوم ووقت مختوم. والخلق يموتون أو يقتلون بآجالهم. وقد كثر تخبط المبتدعة في ذلك. فزعم زاعمون منهم: أن من قتل لو ترك لمات، وقاتله قاطع أجله. ولذلك يقتل من قتله. وهذا يدرأه كلام قريب. فنقول: الأجل: عبارة عن وقت حدث من الأحداث، فاذا علم الله تبارك وتعالى أن انسانا سيقتل فلابد من وقوع معلومه. فان قيل: كان يجوز أن لا يقتل ويبقى. قلنا: ان كان فى علم الله تبارك وتعالى أنه يقتل. فانه يقتل لا محالة. ولو قيل: لو علم الله تبارك وتعالى أنه لا يقتل لبقى. قلنا: هذا التقدير لا ينضبط، اذ كان يجوز أن يقع فى معلومه أنه لا يقتل. ويموت من ساعته حتف أنفه. والذى يموت من غير قتل كان يجوز أن يبقى دهرا. فلو فتحت أبواب التجويزات لما استقر لشيء أجل في علم الله. فهذا القدر كاف في الآجال.
Chapter on Lifespans and Provisions. For every coming-to-be and passing-away, remaining and perishing, life and death: there is a fixed term and an appointed time. Creatures die or are killed at their appointed terms. The innovators have greatly erred in this. So some claimants among them claimed that one who is killed, if left alone, would have died, and his killer cuts his term short. Therefore, whoever kills him, kills him. This is refuted by a brief statement. We say: The term (ajal) is an expression for the time of an event. So if Allah, blessed and exalted, knows that a person will be killed, then His knowledge must occur. If it is said: It was possible that he would not be killed and would remain. We say: If it is in Allah's knowledge that he will be killed, then he will be killed without fail. And if it were said: If Allah knew that he would not be killed, he would remain. We say: This supposition is not fixed, since it is possible that it occurs in His knowledge that he will not be killed. And one who dies of natural causes, it was possible that he would remain for a long time. So if the doors of possibilities were opened, no term would be fixed in Allah's knowledge. This suffices concerning lifespans.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument about the nature of the lifespan (ajal). The author begins by asserting that everything has a fixed term. He then identifies the innovator claim: that the killer cuts the term short, implying the victim would have lived longer if not killed. The refutation is clear: ajal is defined as the time of the event as known by God. If God knows a person will be killed, then that is his term; it is impossible that he would live longer. Similarly, if one dies naturally, God knew he would die at that time. The author closes by warning that if we entertain possibilities contrary to God's knowledge, no term would be fixed.

Key Terms
الأجل
المبتدعة
العلم
التجويز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That if someone is killed, they would have lived longer if not killed; so killer cuts lifespan short.
Correction: The lifespan is defined by God's knowledge. If God knows the person will be killed, that death is their fixed term. It is impossible they would have lived longer.

Checkpoint
How does Juwayni define the term (ajal) in this passage?
A) The moment of death as decreed by God
B) The time of death as known by God
C) The length of life from birth to death
D) The appointed time for killing

Key Takeaway
Juwayni demonstrates that the term (ajal) is the time of death as known by God, so no act, including killing, can alter it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Fixed Terms and Refutation of Premature Death
Juwayni defines ajāl and refutes the claim that killing cuts the term.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's definition of ajal (fixed term) and how he refutes the claim that killing cuts a person's term.

Core Idea
God's knowledge determines each creature's term; no act can change what He knows.

Juwayni addresses a subtle but dangerous error: the idea that if someone is killed, the killer truly ends their life, implying a deficiency in divine decree. He begins by clarifying the very meaning of 'term' and then shows why such objections are logically incoherent. This passage is a classic kalam argument defending God's omniscience and the fixity of destiny.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Juwayni uses a concise, argumentative style here.
2
Identify Juwayni's definition of ajal
Find the sentence where Juwayni defines 'ajal'. Notice that he defines it as 'the time of an occurrence' and links it to God's knowledge.
This definition is key to the entire argument.
3
Understand the innovators' objection
Look for the claim that 'whoever is killed, if left, would have died' and that the killer 'cuts' the term. What does this objection imply about God's decree?
The objection suggests that killing prematurely ends a life, contradicting predestination.
4
Follow Juwayni's refutation
Trace the logical steps: if God knows a person will be killed, it must happen. Hypotheticals about not being killed are irrelevant because God's knowledge is fixed.
Juwayni uses the principle that God's knowledge is infallible and determines reality.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Juwayni warns that if we allow possibilities to override knowledge, nothing would have a fixed term. Understand why this protects divine omniscience.
This reinforces the traditional Ash'ari view of qadar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فى الأجال والارزاق لكل حدوث وعدم ، وبقاء وفناء ، وحياة وممات : أجل معلوم ووقت مختوم . والخلق يموتون أو يقتلون بآجالهم . وقد كثر تخبط المبتدعة في ذلك . فزعم زاعمون منهم : أن من قتل لو ترك لمات ، وقاتله قاطع أجله . وهذا يدرأه كلام قريب . فنقول : الأجل : عبارة عن وقت حدث من الأحداث ، فاذا علم الله تبارك وتعالى أن انسانا سيقتل فلابد من وقوع معلومه . فان قيل : كان يجوز أن لا يقتل ويبقى . قلنا : ان كان فى علم الله تبارك وتعالى أنه يقتل . فانه يقتل لا محالة . ولو قيل : لو علم الله تبارك وتعالى أنه لا يقتل لبقى . قلنا : هذا التقدير لا ينضبط • اذ كان يجوز : أن يقع فى معلومه أنه لا يقتل . والذي يموت من غير قتل كان يجوز أن يبقى دهرا . فلو فتحت أبواب التجويزات لما استقر لشيء أجل في علم الله . فهذا القدر كاف في الآجال
Chapter on terms and provisions. Every occurrence and non-existence, permanence and annihilation, life and death has a known term and a sealed time. Creatures die or are killed by their terms. The innovators have greatly fluctuated in this. Some of them claimed: 'Whoever is killed, if left, would have died, and his killer is the one who cuts his term.' This is refuted by a close argument. So we say: The term (ajal) is an expression for the time of an occurrence. If God, blessed and exalted, knows that a person will be killed, then what He knows must occur. If it is said: 'It could be that he is not killed and remains,' we say: If it is in God's knowledge that he will be killed, then he will inevitably be killed. And if it is said: 'If God knew that he would not be killed, he would remain,' we say: This estimation is not fixed, because it is possible that what is known is that he will not be killed. And the one who dies without being killed could have remained for a long time. If the doors of possibilities were opened, no thing's term would be established in God's knowledge. This is sufficient concerning terms.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of ajal (fixed term) and refutes an objection from heretics who claim that killing someone prematurely cuts their term. Juwayni begins by stating that everything has a predetermined term. He then identifies a deviant view: that if someone is killed, they would have died anyway naturally, and the killer merely cuts the term. This implies the killer is the one who ends the life, not God. Juwayni rejects this by defining ajal as the time of an event as known by God. If God knows that a person will be killed, that event is inevitable. If the objector posits a scenario where the person might not be killed and live longer, Juwayni responds that such hypotheticals are irrelevant because God's knowledge determines reality. He concludes that if we allowed all possibilities, nothing would have a fixed term in God's knowledge. The argument relies on divine omniscience and the impossibility of altering God's knowledge.

Key Terms
أجل
الأجال
الموت
القتل
علم الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That a murder victim's death is solely caused by the killer, not by God's decree.
Correction: Juwayni shows that even if someone is killed, they die at their appointed term as known by God. The killer is an instrument, not the ultimate cause.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what is the definition of 'ajal' (term)?
A) The lifespan of a person from birth to natural death.
B) The expression for the time of an occurrence, as known by God.
C) The moment of death caused by illness or old age.
D) The predetermined lifespan that cannot be changed by any means.

Key Takeaway
Ajal is the time of an event as known by God; all deaths, whether natural or violent, occur at their appointed term according to God's knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Juwayni says that if God knows you will be killed, then you will inevitably be killed. Do you truly believe that every moment of your life is in God's hands, even the most violent or unexpected? What would change in your daily anxiety if you internalized that nothing can shorten your term?
?
The innovators thought the killer 'cuts the term'—they feared human evil could override God's decree. Are there areas in your life where you fear circumstances or people more than you trust God's decree? How can you actively surrender that fear to God's knowledge?
?
Juwayni warns that if we open the doors of possibilities, no term is fixed. Do you live as if your term is fixed, or do you act as if you have endless tomorrows? If you knew your exact moment of death, how would you spend your next hour? What is stopping you from living that way now?

Definition and Division of Provision
Juwayni defines rizq and divides it into halal, haram, and non-moral.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's broad definition of provision (rizq) and its threefold division into halal, haram, and non-moral categories.

Core Idea
Provision is anything beneficial, whether halal or haram.

In this passage, Imam al-Juwayni lays the groundwork for understanding divine sustenance. He begins by defining rizq in the broadest possible terms, then immediately clarifies that it includes both lawful and unlawful means. This definition is crucial for refuting later misunderstandings about who is sustained by God.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition and division
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice that the definition of rizq is anything from which a beneficiary benefits. Then observe how Juwayni divides it into three categories: halal, haram, and non-moral.
The non-moral category includes provisions for animals, which are not subject to religious law.
2
Identify the key terms
Focus on the Arabic terms 'رزق' (provision), 'حلال' (lawful), 'حرام' (unlawful), and 'الرازق' (the Provider). Understand their meanings in this context.
3
Understand the theological significance
Reflect on why this broad definition matters. It establishes that all beneficial things, even if acquired sinfully, are still provisions from God. This sets the stage for the next lesson on the inclusion of wrongdoers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الرزق : فكل ما انتفع به منتفع فهو رزقه . ثم الرزق ينقسم الى الحلال والحرام، والى ما لا يتصف بالتحليل والتحريم كرزق البهائم فالله الرازق ، ولا رازق غيره ، ولا خالق سواه . ثم أنه تبارك وتعالى قسم أرزاق العباد حلالا وحراما ، كما صرفهم بحكمة فى الطاعات والزلات ، توفيقا وخذلانا ، وعطاء وحرمانا . ومن زعم أن الظلمة والذين يتعاطون الحرام ليسوا فى رزق الله ، فقد أخرج معظم الخلائق فى معظم الأوقات عن كونهم مرتزقة الله تعالى . وقال تبارك وتعالى : ( وما من دابة فى الأرض الا على الله رزقها ) هود : ٦
As for provision (rizq): everything from which a beneficiary benefits is his provision. Then provision is divided into halal and haram, and into that which is not characterized by lawfulness and unlawfulness, like the provision of beasts. So God is the Provider, and there is no provider other than Him, and no creator besides Him. Then He, blessed and exalted, divided the provisions of servants into halal and haram, just as He turned them with wisdom in acts of obedience and slips, granting success and abandoning, giving and depriving. And whoever claims that the wrongdoers and those who commit haram are not in God's provision has excluded most of creation, in most times, from being sustained by God Almighty. And He, blessed and exalted, said: 'And there is no creature on earth but that upon God is its provision' (Hud: 6).
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage defines rizq (provision) and clarifies its scope. Juwayni first gives a broad definition: anything from which a beneficiary gains benefit is his provision. This includes both lawful and unlawful means. He then divides provision into three categories: halal, haram, and that which is not subject to legal classification, such as the provision of animals (which are not morally accountable). Next, he emphasizes that God alone is the Provider (al-Rāziq) and Creator. He then addresses a heretical view: that wrongdoers and those who engage in haram (e.g., through usurpation) are not sustained by God. Juwayni refutes this by pointing out that such a claim would exclude most people at most times from God's sustenance, which contradicts the Qur'anic verse 'And there is no creature on earth but that upon God is its provision' (Hud: 6). This verse establishes that all creatures are sustained by God, regardless of their actions.

Key Terms
رزق
حلال
حرام
الرازق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what is the definition of 'rizq' (provision)?
A) Only that which is halal and lawful.
B) Everything from which a beneficiary benefits, whether halal or haram.
C) Only the food and drink that sustain life.
D) That which is created by God and given to believers only.

Key Takeaway
Provision is defined broadly as any benefit, and it includes both lawful and unlawful means, with only God as the Provider.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every benefit you receive—whether from a lawful source or an unlawful one—comes only from God? If so, how does that change your fear of missing out on halal provision?
?
When you consume something that is haram, do you recognize it as provision from God, yet still repent and avoid it? How can you increase your reliance on God alone for lawful provision?
?
If provision includes even the grass the animal eats, can you truly say you lack anything? What does that reveal about your trust in God's role as ar-Razzaq?

Refuting Denial of Provision to Wrongdoers
Juwayni refutes the view that wrongdoers are not in God's provision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's refutation of the claim that wrongdoers are not sustained by God, and his use of Qur'an 11:6.

Core Idea
Even wrongdoers are sustained by God — exclusion contradicts the Qur'an.

After defining provision broadly, Juwayni addresses a common misconception that those who engage in haram are not actually receiving provision from God. He refutes this by logical consequence and by quoting the Qur'an. This lesson examines that refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation argument
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Pay attention to how Juwayni frames the argument: 'And whoever claims...' followed by the consequence.
2
Analyze the logical consequence
Consider why the claim that wrongdoers are not in God's provision would 'exclude most of creation, in most times.' Think about the proportion of people who commit wrongdoings.
This highlights the absurdity of the claim.
3
See the Qur'anic proof
Reflect on the verse from Surah Hud (11:6) and how it serves as a decisive proof that every creature's provision is from God, regardless of its actions.

Divine Decree

Juwayni on God's Creation of Good and Evil
Affirms God's absolute power over good and evil and His immunity from harm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's affirmation that God is the sole creator of good and evil, that He is transcendent above benefit or harm, and that His power extends to everything rationally possible.

Core Idea
God creates good and evil, but is harmed by neither.

This lesson explores a central Ash'ari doctrine: that God creates all actions, including evil. Juwayni explains that God is completely unaffected by what He creates—He neither benefits from good nor suffers from evil. Only creatures experience benefit or harm. The passage also grounds this in rational possibility: whatever reason deems possible, God has power over.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic text and its English translation carefully. Pay attention to the flow from the general statement to the specific quote.
The passage includes both Juwayni's own words and a direct quotation.
2
Identify the key claims
Notice that Juwayni makes two main points: (1) God creates both good and evil without being affected, and (2) God's power covers everything that reason considers possible.
3
Reflect on divine transcendence
Consider why it is important that God is not harmed by evil or benefited by good. This guards against anthropomorphic conceptions of God.
This connects to the doctrine of tanzih (transcendence).
4
Understand the rational principle
Juwayni's principle 'everything reason deems permissible and possible' shows that God's power is not limited by our experience—only by logical impossibility.
This is a foundational rule in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتحدث الجويني - رحمه الله - عن خلق الله تعالى للخير والشر فأثبت أن الله تعالى خالق للخير والشر ولا يتضرر بالشر كما لا ينتفع بنقيضه وهو الخير . وانما يتضرر العباد وينتفعون . ولو أراد احداث خير أو شر فى العالم بغير واسطة أو بواسطة بشر فانه لا راد لارادته . يقول : . » كل ما قضى العقل بجوازه وامكان حدوثه فالرب تعالى موصوف بالاقتدار عليه ، ولو فرض احداثه اياه كان مسوغا في العقل غير ممتنع » وهذا أمر متفق عليه بين أهل الشرائع ففى القرآن الكريم
And Al-Juwayni — may Allah have mercy on him — spoke about Allah Almighty's creation of good and evil, so he affirmed that Allah Almighty is the Creator of good and evil, and He is not harmed by evil just as He does not benefit from its opposite, which is good. Rather, the servants are harmed and benefit. And if He willed to bring about good or evil in the world without an intermediary or through a human intermediary, then there is no repeller of His will. He says: 'Everything that reason deems permissible and possible to occur, the Lord Almighty is described as having power over it. And if His bringing it about is assumed, it would be permissible in reason, not impossible.' And this is a matter agreed upon among the people of religions, for in the Holy Quran...
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage presents Juwayni's position on the divine decree (qadar). He asserts that God is the sole creator of both good and evil, but He is entirely unaffected by them — He neither benefits from good nor is harmed by evil. Instead, creatures are the ones who experience benefit or harm. God's will is absolute and irresistible; no one can thwart His intention to bring about any event, whether directly or through human means. Juwayni then provides a philosophical formulation: whenever reason deems something possible, God has power over it, and its occurrence is rationally permissible. He claims this view is agreed upon by all religious communities, citing the Quran (though the quote is cut off). The passage defends the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb (acquisition) and divine omnipotence.

خير
شر
اقتدار
إرادة
جواز عقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God creates evil, He is harmed by it, or that He only creates good.
Correction: Juwayni clarifies that God is transcendent above benefit and harm; He creates both good and evil without being affected by them.

Checkpoint

A) Only good
B) Only evil
C) Everything that reason deems possible
D) Only what occurs naturally

Key Takeaway
God creates all possible things, including good and evil, and remains transcendent above all benefit and harm.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience evil or hardship, do you truly believe that Allah created it and is not harmed by it? Or do you sometimes feel that Allah is distant or unaware of your pain? How can you train your heart to see both good and evil as coming from Him, without resentment?
?
If Allah is not affected by your good deeds or your sins, why should you strive to obey Him? Does this truth increase your love for Him because He is self-sufficient, or does it make you feel disconnected? Answer honestly.
?
Since Allah's power is absolute and no one can repulse His will, what does that mean for your worries about the future? Are you truly submitting to His decree, or are you still trying to control outcomes? What is one specific area you need to surrender to Him today?

Juwayni's Description of Divine Tawfiq and Khatm
Juwayni describes the mechanisms of tawfiq and khatm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's account of how Allah grants success to believers and seals the hearts of disbelievers, all by eternal decree.

Core Idea
Tawfiq and khatm are direct results of Allah's eternal will, not responses to human choice.

Juwayni explains that when Allah wills good for a servant, He facilitates every means of obedience; when He wills evil, He distances the servant from good and seals the heart. This passage presents his deterministic theology in vivid detail.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the contrasting descriptions for those whom Allah wills good versus evil.
Pay attention to the list of facilitations for good and impediments for evil.
2
Identify the elements for each case
List the specific things Allah does when He wills good (perfecting intellect, removing obstacles, etc.) and when He wills evil (distancing from good, making sin desirable, etc.).
3
Reflect on the role of divine decree
Note that Juwayni concludes by attributing the sealing to 'the decree of Allah and His destiny.' Consider how this frames all events as predetermined.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتحدث الجويني عن توفيق الله للطائعين ، وطبعه وختمه على قلوب المعتدين والكافرين . فيقول » اذا أراد الله بعبد خيرا أكمل عقله ، وأتم بصيرته ثم صرف عنه العوائق والدوافع ، وأزاح عنه الموانع ، ووفق له قرناء الخير وسهل له سبيله ، وقطع عنه الملهيات وأسباب الغفلات والذهول ، وقيض له ما يقرب الى القربات فيألفيها ، ثم يعتادها ، ويمرن عليها . واذا أراد بعبد شرا قدر له ما يبعده عن الخير ويقصيه ، وهيأ له تماديه فى الغى ، وحبب اليه التشوق الى الشهوات ، وعرضه للآفات .. وكلما غلبت دواعى الشر خنست دواعى الخير ، ثم يستمر على الشرور على مر الدهور ، هاويا في مهاويها ، وتتعاون عليه الوساوس ، ونزغات الشيطان ونزوات النفس الأمارة بالسوء فتنشيء الغفلة غشاوة على قلبه ، بقضاء الله تبارك وتعالى وقدره ، فذلكم الطبع - عافاكم الله - والختم والأكنة ) . لقد أرجع التوفيق والطبع والختم الى « بقضاء الله تبارك وتعالى وقدره » انه لم يثبت اختيارا فى أفعال العباد - خلافا لما فهم الشيخ الأمام زاهد الكوثرى - لم يثبت ارادة خيرة من العبد بسببها يوقفه الله ولم يثبت ارادة سيئة من العبد بسببها يطبع الله على قلبه . انه سار في أفعال العباد وفى القضاء والقدر المؤديان في نظره الى التوفيق والطبع الى ما أراده الله أزلا من العالم . فالعالم يسير حسب خطة رسمها الله فى الأزل كما يقرر . ولو أنه قرر في آية التوفيق وآيات الطبع أن الله تعالى اذا رأى من العبد اتجاها الى الخيرات وفقه الى الخيرات . واذا رأى منه اتجاها الى المنكرات خلى بينه وبين نفسه الأمارة بالسوء . لكان بهذا التقرير موضحا لعدل الله ورحمته وأنه ما يريد ظلما للعباد .
And al-Juwayni speaks about Allah's granting success (tawfiq) to the obedient, and His sealing and stamping (khatm) upon the hearts of the transgressors and disbelievers. He says: 'When Allah wills good for a servant, He perfects his intellect, completes his insight, then averts from him obstacles and motives, removes barriers, provides for him good companions, eases his path, cuts off from him distractions and causes of heedlessness and forgetfulness, and appoints for him what brings him near to acts of devotion so he becomes familiar with them, then accustoms himself to them and practices them. And when He wills evil for a servant, He decrees for him what distances him from good and keeps him away, prepares for him persistence in error, makes desirable to him longing for passions, and exposes him to afflictions... And whenever the motives of evil dominate, the motives of good recede, then he continues in evils over the ages, falling into their abysses, and whisperings, satanic temptations, and impulses of the soul commanding evil cooperate against him, so heedlessness produces a covering over his heart, by the decree (qada) of Allah, blessed and exalted, and His destiny (qadr). That is the sealing—may Allah protect you—the stamping and the covering.' He has indeed attributed tawfiq, sealing, and stamping to 'the decree of Allah, blessed and exalted, and His destiny.' He did not establish any choice in the actions of servants—contrary to what Shaykh Imam Zahid al-Kawthari understood. He did not establish a good will from the servant for which Allah grants him success, nor an evil will from the servant for which Allah stamps his heart. He proceeded in the actions of servants and in the decree and destiny that lead in his view to tawfiq and sealing to what Allah willed from eternity for the world. So the world proceeds according to a plan that Allah drew up in eternity, as he determines. And if he had determined in the verses of tawfiq and the verses of stamping that Allah, exalted, when He sees a direction towards good from the servant, grants him success towards good, and when He sees a direction towards evil from him, He leaves him to his soul commanding evil, then by this determination he would have clarified the justice and mercy of Allah and that He does not will injustice for the servants.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
In this passage, the author presents al-Juwayni's description of divine tawfiq (granting success) and khatm (sealing of hearts). Al-Juwayni explains that when Allah wills good for a servant, He perfects his intellect, removes obstacles, provides good companions, and facilitates obedience. Conversely, when He wills evil, He distances the servant from good, makes sin attractive, and allows heedlessness to cover the heart—all by divine decree and destiny. The author then critiques al-Juwayni's view, arguing that he reduces everything to divine decree without any genuine human choice or will. According to the author, al-Juwayni does not posit a prior human inclination that triggers divine action; rather, tawfiq and sealing are direct results of what Allah willed from eternity. The author suggests that if al-Juwayni had instead taught that Allah responds to the servant's direction—granting success when He sees good intent, and leaving him when He sees evil intent—then this would better demonstrate divine justice and mercy. Thus, the passage is both an exposition and a critique of al-Juwayni's deterministic interpretation of key Qur'anic concepts.

Key Terms
توفيق
طبع
ختم
قضاء
قدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Juwayni's view of tawfiq allows for human initiative; the passage shows he traces everything back to eternal divine decree.
Correction: Juwayni explicitly attributes tawfiq and khatm to 'the decree of Allah and His destiny,' without mentioning any prior human action.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what happens when Allah wills good for a servant?
A) He leaves him to his own devices.
B) He perfects his intellect and removes obstacles.
C) He tests him with hardships.
D) He seals his heart.

Key Takeaway
Juwayni attributes both tawfiq and khatm entirely to Allah's eternal decree without reference to human initiative.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When Juwayni says that Allah perfects the intellect and completes insight for those He wills good for, does that make you feel that your own efforts to seek knowledge and righteousness are irrelevant? Or does it press you to beg Allah for His tawfiq with greater urgency?
?
If the sealing of hearts is part of Allah's eternal decree and not a response to your choices, what keeps you from falling into despair when you struggle with sin? How does this truth shape your daily supplication?
?
Juwayni attributes both the believer's guidance and the disbeliever's misguidance directly to Allah's will. If you truly believe this, does it not shatter all pride in your good deeds? How will you live differently tonight because of this?

Critique of Juwayni's Deterministic View
The author critiques Juwayni's deterministic view and proposes an alternative based on divine justice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's critique that Juwayni's explanation of tawfiq and khatm eliminates genuine human choice and fails to uphold divine justice.

Core Idea
True divine justice requires that Allah responds to human direction, not that He predestines both obedience and disobedience without regard to human will.

The author argues that Juwayni's deterministic model, where tawfiq and khatm are decreed from eternity, does not account for any real human will or choice. He suggests an alternative interpretation that better aligns with God's justice and mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the critique carefully
Read the Arabic then the translation. Note the author's assertion that Juwayni did not establish any choice in the actions of servants.
Focus on the phrase 'lam yuthbit ikhtiyaran fi af'al al-'ibad'.
2
Identify the missing element
The author says Juwayni did not establish a good or evil will from the servant that would be the basis for tawfiq or khatm. This is the key absence.
3
Consider the proposed alternative
The author suggests that if Juwayni had said Allah grants success when He sees good direction and leaves the servant when He sees evil direction, it would better demonstrate justice and mercy.

ويتحدث الجويني عن توفيق الله للطائعين ، وطبعه وختمه على قلوب المعتدين والكافرين . فيقول » اذا أراد الله بعبد خيرا أكمل عقله ، وأتم بصيرته ثم صرف عنه العوائق والدوافع ، وأزاح عنه الموانع ، ووفق له قرناء الخير وسهل له سبيله ، وقطع عنه الملهيات وأسباب الغفلات والذهول ، وقيض له ما يقرب الى القربات فيألفيها ، ثم يعتادها ، ويمرن عليها . واذا أراد بعبد شرا قدر له ما يبعده عن الخير ويقصيه ، وهيأ له تماديه فى الغى ، وحبب اليه التشوق الى الشهوات ، وعرضه للآفات .. وكلما غلبت دواعى الشر خنست دواعى الخير ، ثم يستمر على الشرور على مر الدهور ، هاويا في مهاويها ، وتتعاون عليه الوساوس ، ونزغات الشيطان ونزوات النفس الأمارة بالسوء فتنشيء الغفلة غشاوة على قلبه ، بقضاء الله تبارك وتعالى وقدره ، فذلكم الطبع - عافاكم الله - والختم والأكنة ) . لقد أرجع التوفيق والطبع والختم الى « بقضاء الله تبارك وتعالى وقدره » انه لم يثبت اختيارا فى أفعال العباد - خلافا لما فهم الشيخ الأمام زاهد الكوثرى - لم يثبت ارادة خيرة من العبد بسببها يوقفه الله ولم يثبت ارادة سيئة من العبد بسببها يطبع الله على قلبه . انه سار في أفعال العباد وفى القضاء والقدر المؤديان في نظره الى التوفيق والطبع الى ما أراده الله أزلا من العالم . فالعالم يسير حسب خطة رسمها الله فى الأزل كما يقرر . ولو أنه قرر في آية التوفيق وآيات الطبع أن الله تعالى اذا رأى من العبد اتجاها الى الخيرات وفقه الى الخيرات . واذا رأى منه اتجاها الى المنكرات خلى بينه وبين نفسه الأمارة بالسوء . لكان بهذا التقرير موضحا لعدل الله ورحمته وأنه ما يريد ظلما للعباد .
And al-Juwayni speaks about Allah's granting success (tawfiq) to the obedient, and His sealing and stamping (khatm) upon the hearts of the transgressors and disbelievers. He says: 'When Allah wills good for a servant, He perfects his intellect, completes his insight, then averts from him obstacles and motives, removes barriers, provides for him good companions, eases his path, cuts off from him distractions and causes of heedlessness and forgetfulness, and appoints for him what brings him near to acts of devotion so he becomes familiar with them, then accustoms himself to them and practices them. And when He wills evil for a servant, He decrees for him what distances him from good and keeps him away, prepares for him persistence in error, makes desirable to him longing for passions, and exposes him to afflictions... And whenever the motives of evil dominate, the motives of good recede, then he continues in evils over the ages, falling into their abysses, and whisperings, satanic temptations, and impulses of the soul commanding evil cooperate against him, so heedlessness produces a covering over his heart, by the decree (qada) of Allah, blessed and exalted, and His destiny (qadr). That is the sealing—may Allah protect you—the stamping and the covering.' He has indeed attributed tawfiq, sealing, and stamping to 'the decree of Allah, blessed and exalted, and His destiny.' He did not establish any choice in the actions of servants—contrary to what Shaykh Imam Zahid al-Kawthari understood. He did not establish a good will from the servant for which Allah grants him success, nor an evil will from the servant for which Allah stamps his heart. He proceeded in the actions of servants and in the decree and destiny that lead in his view to tawfiq and sealing to what Allah willed from eternity for the world. So the world proceeds according to a plan that Allah drew up in eternity, as he determines. And if he had determined in the verses of tawfiq and the verses of stamping that Allah, exalted, when He sees a direction towards good from the servant, grants him success towards good, and when He sees a direction towards evil from him, He leaves him to his soul commanding evil, then by this determination he would have clarified the justice and mercy of Allah and that He does not will injustice for the servants.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
In this passage, the author presents al-Juwayni's description of divine tawfiq (granting success) and khatm (sealing of hearts). Al-Juwayni explains that when Allah wills good for a servant, He perfects his intellect, removes obstacles, provides good companions, and facilitates obedience. Conversely, when He wills evil, He distances the servant from good, makes sin attractive, and allows heedlessness to cover the heart—all by divine decree and destiny. The author then critiques al-Juwayni's view, arguing that he reduces everything to divine decree without any genuine human choice or will. According to the author, al-Juwayni does not posit a prior human inclination that triggers divine action; rather, tawfiq and sealing are direct results of what Allah willed from eternity. The author suggests that if al-Juwayni had instead taught that Allah responds to the servant's direction—granting success when He sees good intent, and leaving him when He sees evil intent—then this would better demonstrate divine justice and mercy. Thus, the passage is both an exposition and a critique of al-Juwayni's deterministic interpretation of key Qur'anic concepts.

Key Terms
اختيار
عدل
رحمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the author's alternative still denies human freedom; the passage shows he advocates for a responsive divine action based on the servant's direction.
Correction: The author says Allah sees a direction from the servant and then grants success or leaves him, which implies a role for human initiative.

Checkpoint
What does the author say is missing from Juwayni's explanation of tawfiq and khatm?
A) Divine decree.
B) Human will and choice.
C) The importance of good deeds.
D) The power of the servant.

Key Takeaway
The author contends that true justice requires acknowledging that Allah grants success or seals hearts in response to the servant's direction, not solely by eternal decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you find yourself blaming 'fate' or 'that's just how Allah made me' instead of owning your direction? What would change if you truly believed that Allah seals hearts only after He sees an evil direction from you?
?
Are you consciously directing your heart towards good, expecting Allah's tawfiq, or do you passively assume that whatever happens was always destined? Examine your daily choices—how often do you intentionally seek Allah's response?
?
If you really believe that Allah's justice responds to your direction, what will you do differently today to ensure He sees a direction towards good? Be specific: one concrete action you will take within the next hour.

Divine Decree
intermediate
5 min
Juwayni's Account of Tawfiq and Tab'
Juwayni describes the divine mechanism of tawfiq and tab'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's detailed description of how God decrees success (tawfiq) for the obedient and sealing (tab') for the disbelievers, attributing both entirely to His eternal will.

Core Idea
God's decree directly causes both guidance and misguidance.

Imam al-Juwayni presents a vivid picture of divine intervention in human destiny. He explains that when God wills good for a servant, He removes obstacles and facilitates obedience; when He wills evil, He seals the heart. This passage shows a deterministic framework where all outcomes are directly ordained by God.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, focusing on Juwayni's two scenarios: for the obedient and for the disbeliever.
Notice the parallel structure in describing God's actions.
2
Identify key divine actions
List the actions God takes in each scenario (e.g., perfects intellect, removes obstacles, appoints companions; distances from good, makes evil desirable).
These actions are all directly attributed to God's decree.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Juwayni ends by saying this sealing is 'by the decree of God.' Ask: what does this imply about human choice?
This sets up the critique in the next lesson.

القدرة الحادثة ، ويستحيل أن يقع بعضه بقدرة الله عز وجل ، فان الفعل الواحد لا بعض له

ويتحدث الجويني عن توفيق الله للطائعين ، وطبعه وختمه على قلوب المعتدين والكافرين . فيقول » اذا أراد الله بعبد خيرا أكمل عقله ، وأتم بصيرته ثم صرف عنه العوائق والدوافع ، وأزاح عنه الموانع ، ووفق لــه قرناء الخير وسهل له سبيله ، وقطع عنه الملهيات وأسباب الغفلات والذهول ، وقيض له ما يقرب الى القربات فيألفيها ، ثم يعتادها ، ويمرن عليها . واذا أراد بعبد شرا قدر له ما يبعده عن الخير ويقصيه ، وهيأ له تماديه فى الغى ، وحبب اليه التشوق الى الشهوات ، وعرضه للآفات .. وكلما غلبت دواعى الشر خنست دواعى الخير ، ثم يستمر على الشرور على مر الدهور ، هاويا في مهاويها ، وتتعاون عليه الوساوس ، ونزغات الشيطان ونزوات النفس الأمارة بالسوء فتنشيء الغفلة غشاوة على قلبه ، بقضاء الله تبارك وتعالى وقدره ، فذلكم الطبع - عافاكم الله - والختم والأكنة ) .

لقد أرجع التوفيق والطبع والختم الى « بقضاء الله تبارك وتعالى وقدره » انه لم يثبت اختيارا فى أفعال العباد - خلافا لما فهم الشيخ الأمام زاهد الكوثرى - لم يثبت ارادة خيرة من العبد بسببها يوقفه الله ولم يثبت ارادة سيئة من العبد بسببها يطبع الله على قلبه . انه سار في أفعال العباد وفى القضاء والقدر المؤديان في نظره الى التوفيق والطبع الى ما أراده الله أزلا من العالم . فالعالم يسير حسب خطة رسمها الله فى الأزل كما يقرر . ولو أنه قرر في آية التوفيق وآيات الطبع أن الله تعالى اذا رأى من العبد اتجاها الى الخيرات وفقه الى الخيرات . واذا رأى منه اتجاها الى المنكرات خلى بينه وبين نفسه الأمارة بالسوء . لكان بهذا التقرير موضحا لعدل الله ورحمته وأنه ما يريد ظلما للعباد .
The created power, and it is impossible that part of it occurs by the power of God Almighty, for a single action has no parts.

And Juwayni discusses God's granting of success (tawfiq) to the obedient, and His sealing (tab') and stamping (khatm) upon the hearts of the transgressors and disbelievers. He says: 'When God desires for a servant good, He perfects his intellect, completes his insight, then removes from him obstacles and impediments, and clears away hindrances, and appoints for him companions of good and eases his way, and cuts off from him distractions and causes of heedlessness and forgetfulness, and prepares for him what brings him near to acts of devotion so that he becomes familiar with them, then accustoms himself to them, and practices them. And when He desires for a servant evil, He decrees for him what distances him from good and keeps him away, and prepares for him persistence in error, and makes desirable to him yearning for desires, and exposes him to afflictions. And whenever the motives of evil prevail, the motives of good retreat, then he continues in evils over the course of ages, falling into their abysses, and whisperings and the promptings of Satan and the impulses of the soul commanding evil cooperate against him, so heedlessness creates a covering over his heart, by the decree of God Almighty and His predestination. So that is the sealing (tab') — may God preserve you — and the stamping (khatm) and the covering (akina).'

He indeed attributed tawfiq, tab', and khatm to 'the decree of God Almighty and His predestination.' He did not establish any choice in the actions of servants — contrary to what Shaykh Imam Zahid al-Kawthari understood — he did not establish any good will from the servant by which God would grant him success, nor did he establish any evil will from the servant by which God would seal his heart. He proceeded in the actions of servants and in the decree and predestination that in his view lead to tawfiq and tab' according to what God willed from eternity concerning the world. So the world proceeds according to a plan that God drew up in eternity, as he asserts. And if he had stated in the verse of tawfiq and the verses of tab' that God Almighty, when He sees from the servant a direction towards good, grants him success towards good, and when He sees from him a direction towards evil, leaves him alone with his soul commanding evil, then by this statement he would have clarified God's justice and mercy and that He does not desire injustice for the servants.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage begins with a brief statement on created power (qudra haditha), asserting that it is impossible for a single action to be partially caused by God's power because an action is indivisible. Then the commentator introduces Juwayni's discussion of God's tawfiq (granting success) for the obedient and His tab' and khatm (sealing) for the wrongdoers. Juwayni is quoted describing how God, when He wills good for a servant, perfects his intellect and removes obstacles, appoints good companions, and facilitates obedience. Conversely, when He wills evil, He distances the servant from good, makes sin attractive, and allows whispers and Satanic promptings to overwhelm him, ultimately sealing his heart by God's decree and predestination. The commentator then critiques Juwayni, arguing that this view eliminates human choice entirely. Juwayni, according to the commentator, does not attribute tawfiq or sealing to any prior will or action of the servant; rather, everything is directly determined by God's eternal plan. The commentator suggests that if Juwayni had instead said that God responds to the servant's own direction (good or bad), it would better uphold God's justice and mercy.

Key Terms
القدرة الحادثة
التوفيق
الطبع
الختم
القضاء والقدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that in Juwayni's view, human free will plays a role in tawfiq or tab'.
Correction: Juwayni explicitly states that both tawfiq and sealing occur solely by God's decree, with no mention of prior human choice.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni's statement in the passage, what causes the sealing (tab') on a person's heart?
A) The person's own evil choices
B) God's decree and predestination
C) Satan's whisperings alone
D) The person's lack of intellect

Key Takeaway
Juwayni views tawfiq and tab' as direct outcomes of God's eternal decree, with no human initiative.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's decree is the direct cause of your faith, what do you say to yourself when you sin? Do you blame God or take responsibility? How does Juwayni's description challenge your self-perception as an autonomous agent?
?
Juwayni describes God sealing the hearts of the transgressors. Read that description and ask yourself: am I among those who have been sealed? What signs of spiritual blindness do I see in myself? This is a fearful question.
?
The lesson says that when God desires evil for a servant, He facilitates the path to sin. Does this make you complacent or more desperate for God's mercy? How does this truth affect your daily struggle with sin?

Divine Decree

Critique of Juwayni's Determinism
Critique of Juwayni's deterministic view and presentation of an alternative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the critique that Juwayni's view eliminates human choice and fails to uphold divine justice, and the alternative that God responds to human direction.

Core Idea
If God alone decrees all actions, human accountability is lost.

After presenting Juwayni's deterministic account, the commentator offers a sharp critique. He argues that Juwayni's system leaves no room for human will or responsibility. He then proposes an alternative: that God's tawfiq and sealing are responses to the servant's own inclination, not arbitrary decrees. This lesson examines that critique and the proposed alternative.

Guided Path
1
Read the critique passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the critique section. Note the key claims against Juwayni.
The commentator explicitly says Juwayni did not establish any will from the servant.
2
Contrast with the alternative
The commentator suggests an alternative: God sees the servant's direction and then grants success or leaves him alone. Compare this with Juwayni's view.
Note how the alternative preserves human responsibility.
3
Evaluate the implications
Reflect on which view better upholds God's justice and mercy, as the commentator argues.
This is a central debate in Islamic theology.

What does the commentator argue Juwayni failed to do in his account of tawfiq and tab'?
A) Attribute actions to God's power

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial or a failure in faith, do you instinctively attribute it to 'God's decree' in a way that lets you off the hook from examining your own choices? What would change if you first looked at your own direction—your inclinations, your negligence—before invoking qadr?
?
The commentator says God should respond to the servant's direction. Is your life currently moving towards good or evil in a way that would invite God's tawfiq or His leaving you alone? What one concrete sign of 'direction towards good' can you point to in your last week?
?
This lesson shows that a wrong view of qadr can nullify human accountability. Are there areas of your life where you secretly believe that your bad habits or sins are simply 'written' and therefore unchangeable? How would rethinking that as a failure of your own will, not God's decree, change your next step?

Divine Decree

Predetermination of Lifespan and Provision
Juwayni argues that lifespan and provision are predetermined in eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's assertion that both lifespan and provision are predetermined in God's eternal knowledge, and how he supports this with scriptural evidence.

Core Idea
Lifespan and provision are set in eternity, known only to God.

Juwayni begins by establishing that lifespan (ajal) and provision (rizq) are not random or changeable in God's knowledge. He argues that God's foreknowledge necessitates their fixed occurrence, and that provision is universal for all creatures, believers and disbelievers alike. This lesson unpacks his initial claims and their scriptural basis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note that Juwayni uses two key terms: 'ajal' (term) and 'rizq' (provision).
Pay attention to the verse he quotes for provision.
2
Analyze Juwayni's argument for predetermination
Identify the logical flow: if God knows something will happen, it must happen; then he applies this to lifespan and provision.
3
Reflect on the universality of provision
Notice that Juwayni extends provision to both believer and disbeliever, citing the verse about all creatures.

وتحدث الجويني عن الآجال والأرزاق فقال إنهما محددان في الأزل فإذا علم الله تبارك وتعالى أن إنسانا سيقتل فلا بد من وقوع معلومه، وأن الله قسم للمؤمن رزقه، وقسم للكافر رزقه، من قبل أن يوجدا، وأطلق كلمة (الرزق) على المؤمن والكافر، للمفهوم من الآية «وما من دابة في الأرض إلا على الله رزقها» (والكافر دابة والمؤمن دابة). لو كان يجب أن يفرق بين أجل الشهداء، وأجل غير الشهداء فأجل الشهداء محدد في الأزل بقوله تعالى (قل لو كنتم في بيوتكم لبرز الذين كتب عليهم القتل إلى مضاجعهم) (آل عمران: ١٥٤) والمعنى: إن الله كتب قتل من يقتل من المؤمنين، وكتب مع ذلك أنهم الغالبون لعلمه أن العافية في الغلبة لهم وأن دين الإسلام يظهر على الدين كله وأن ما ينكبون من بعض الأوقات تمحيص لهم وترغيب في الشهادة، وحرصهم على الجهاد فتحصل الغلبة. وأجل غير الشهداء غير محدد في الأزل بقوله تعالى (وأنفقوا في سبيل الله ولا تلقوا بأيديكم إلى التهلكة) (البقرة: ١٩٥) والمعنى: النهي عن ترك الإنفاق في سبيل الله، لأنه سبب الهلاك، أو عن الإسراف في النفقة حتى يفقر نفسه ويضيع عياله، أو عن الاقبال والاخطار بالنفس، أو عن ترك الغزو الذي هو تقوية للعدو. ولذلك وجب قتل القاتل لأن في قتله حياة للناس وزجر لسولله نفسه عن القتل في قوله تعالى (ولكم في القصاص حياة) (البقرة: ١٧٩). وأجل غير الشهداء غير محدد أيضا بدليل المشاهد في الحياة من مخلوقات الله فإن إنسانا لو رأى ديكا وجدي ماعز وحصانا لقال إن الديك لو خلي بينه وبين أجله بحسب ما أودع الله في خلايا جسمه من ...
And Juwayni discussed the terms and provisions and said that they are determined in eternity. So when God, blessed and exalted, knows that a human will be killed, then His knowledge must occur. And that God divided the provision for the believer, and divided the provision for the disbeliever, before they existed. And he used the term 'provision' for both the believer and the disbeliever, based on the verse 'And there is no creature on earth except that its provision is upon God.' (Hud: 6) (And the disbeliever is a creature and the believer is a creature). If it were necessary to distinguish between the term of the martyrs and the term of non-martyrs, then the term of the martyrs is predetermined in eternity by His statement: 'Say, even if you were in your houses, those destined for slaughter would go forth to their resting places.' (Al-Imran: 154) The meaning: God wrote the killing of those who are killed among the believers, and also wrote that they are victorious, because He knows that the good outcome is their victory, and that the religion of Islam will prevail over all religion, and that whatever hardships befall them at times are a purification for them and an incentive for martyrdom, and their eagerness for jihad results in victory. And the term of non-martyrs is not predetermined in eternity by His statement: 'And spend in the way of God and do not throw yourselves into destruction.' (Al-Baqara: 195) The meaning: the prohibition of abandoning spending in the way of God because it is a cause of destruction, or overspending so that one impoverishes himself and neglects his dependents, or exposing oneself to danger, or abandoning fighting which strengthens the enemy. Therefore, it is obligatory to kill the killer because in his killing is life for the people and a deterrent for his soul from killing, in His statement: 'And in legal retribution there is life for you.' (Al-Baqara: 179) And the term of non-martyrs is also not predetermined, as evidenced by observation of the creation of God. For if a person sees a rooster, a goat kid, and a horse, he would say that the rooster, if left to its term according to what God has placed in the cells of its body of...
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is Juwayni's exposition on the predetermination of lifespan (ajal) and provision (rizq). He asserts that both are determined in eternity (muḥaddadān fī al-azal). The first point is based on divine foreknowledge: if God knows that a person will be killed, that knowledge must be realized. Then he discusses provision: God has already divided the provision for believers and disbelievers before their existence, using the verse 'There is no creature but its provision is upon God' to show that provision is common to all, not only believers. Then he contrasts the term of martyrs and non-martyrs. The term of martyrs is predetermined based on the verse about those destined for slaughter; the term of non-martyrs is not predetermined, as indicated by the prohibition of self-destruction and the command to spend. He also uses a rational observation: the natural lifespan of animals (like a rooster) is determined by their bodily constitution, implying that human lifespan can also be influenced by causes. This supports the idea that non-martyrs' terms are not rigidly fixed but subject to means (like caution, spending, etc.). However, Juwayni maintains that God's knowledge encompasses everything, so there is a sense of predetermination, but he distinguishes between the fixed term of martyrs and the conditional term of others.

Key Terms
الآجال
الأرزاق
الأزل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Predetermination means humans have no choice or responsibility.
Correction: Juwayni's view is about God's knowledge and decree, not about negating human actions; he later distinguishes between fixed and conditional terms, implying human actions play a role.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, when is provision predetermined?
A) After a person is born
B) At the moment of death
C) In eternity, before existence
D) Only for believers

Key Takeaway
Juwayni establishes that both lifespan and provision are fixed in God's eternal knowledge, without exception for believer or disbeliever.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your lifespan is already determined in eternity, do you truly live each day as if it could be your last? Or do you assume tomorrow is guaranteed? What would change if you acted on this truth today?
?
God has already apportioned your provision before you were born. Why do you still fear scarcity? What does your worry reveal about your trust in God's decree?
?
The passage notes that even the disbeliever receives provision from God. How does this reality challenge your attitude towards those who reject faith? Do you see them as deserving of God's provision? What does that demand of you in your interactions with them?

Divine Decree
intermediate
6 min
The Term of Martyrs vs. Non-Martyrs
Juwayni distinguishes the fixed term of martyrs from the flexible term of non-martyrs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's distinction between the fixed term of martyrs and the flexible term of non-martyrs, and how he uses Quranic verses and rational observation to support this.

Core Idea
Martyrs' term is set; non-martyrs' term can change based on actions.

After establishing general predetermination, Juwayni addresses a potential objection: if terms are fixed, why do martyrs die earlier? He argues that martyrs' terms are indeed fixed in eternity, but non-martyrs' terms are not strictly predetermined; they can be altered by factors like caution, spending, and divine retribution. This lesson examines his evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two categories
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Juwayni contrasts 'the term of martyrs' with 'the term of non-martyrs'.
2
Examine the verses for each category
For martyrs, he quotes 'Those destined for slaughter go forth to their resting places.' For non-martyrs, he quotes 'Do not throw yourselves into destruction' and 'In retribution there is life.'
3
Consider the rational proof for non-martyrs
Juwayni uses an analogy: a rooster's lifespan is determined by its nature, but it can be shortened by external causes. Similarly, a non-martyr's term is not fixed absolutely.
The passage cuts off here; the argument implies conditional predetermination.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If everything is predestined, then human actions like spending or fighting are pointless.
Correction: Juwayni shows that God commands actions that affect lifespan, proving that humans have genuine efficacy within the divine plan.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, which group has a term that is not fixed in eternity?
A) Martyrs
B) Non-martyrs
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Juwayni distinguishes martyrs' fixed term from non-martyrs' conditional term, showing that divine decree accommodates human actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your term is conditional upon your actions, what specific deed are you avoiding or delaying that might be shortening your life or depriving you of a good end?
?
Juwayni says martyrs' terms are fixed, while yours can change. Does the prospect of an uncertain term make you more eager to seek martyrdom, or does it comfort you that you still have time? Examine your heart: which motive is stronger?
?
The command 'do not throw yourselves into destruction' implies you are responsible for preserving your life. In what area of your life are you knowingly risking destruction—whether spiritual, physical, or financial—and what would it cost you to change that today?
